(Nanjing) Gao Bingfang, Director of the Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance, said that the draft income tax regulations is still under review by the central government. The tax revenue has already been included in this year's budget at five million yuan. However, this system is still in its infancy in our country. In order to promote simple taxation and fairness, more consideration is being given to the procedures. Recently, a request has been made to the central government to make a decision as soon as possible so that it can be implemented immediately. Once collection begins, all collection procedures will be handled by the other tax collection agencies under the ministry. The draft estate tax has now been completed but has not yet been sent out. After further study by this ministry, it can be submitted to the Executive Yuan and then to the central government for a decision. It is tentatively set to be levied starting from 5,000 yuan, with tax rates ranging from one per mille to twenty per mille. In addition, as of now, more than 670 counties and cities have submitted their budgets in accordance with central government orders. Based on a calculation of over 1,800 counties nationwide, this represents more than one-third. Because this is the first time that budgets are being handled for the counties and cities, regardless of whether income or expenditure should be included, they are all required to be listed. After review and approval by the ministry, the scope will be indicated, and no other items may be included in the budget thereafter. This time, at least two-thirds can be accomplished. Only remote areas are lacking. After complete verification, the Ministry of Finance will submit it to the Executive Yuan for transmission to the National Government for orders to be followed. If there is any deliberate violation, punishments will be imposed in accordance with Articles 136 and 139 of the new criminal law. (25th Dispatch)

Current Commentary

America's Silver Policy Wavering on the Crossroads 32

— Ting

The U.S. government's silver purchasing policy, since the agreement concluded with China, India, Canada, and others in 1933, has, to this day, caused the New York silver price per ounce to rise from over 30 cents to over 70 cents, and the London silver price per standard ounce to rise from around 18 pence to over 30 pence. During this period, countries using silver, such as China and Mexico, have all suffered from the outflow of silver reserves and monetary contraction. Other countries, such as England, Japan, France, and the Netherlands, have also felt the pain of fluctuating exchange rates. The impact of the silver policy on the world economy can be said to be deep and intense.

Recently, overseas dispatches have reported that Thomas, the new leader of the American silver faction, has vehemently criticized the government's silver purchasing policy, saying that the government's purpose is only to buy silver at the lowest possible price, not to use silver as a genuine currency. He also denounced Pittman, the well-known leader of the silver faction, saying that he is not a spokesman for the silver faction. The U.S. Senate has decided to send committee members such as Thomas to Europe, Asia, and South America after the congressional adjournment to investigate the silver situation, in preparation for efforts to establish new silver legislation when Congress reconvenes in January next year. At the same time, Pittman has also proposed the organization of a five-person committee to investigate the impact of the silver policy on the domestic and international situation in conjunction with the Secretary of the Treasury. These two committees are pursuing their own agendas and clearly have opposing positions, which shows the depth and intensity of the contradictions within the American silver faction. The attitude of the U.S. Treasury Department towards the implementation of the silver purchasing bill has recently been quite different from the beginning, which is particularly noteworthy.

The biggest goal of the silver purchasing bill was originally to create a system of bimetallism in the United States, that is, to make the hard currency reserves for U.S. banknote issuance reach a ratio of three parts gold to one part silver. Although the provisions in the bill at the time were permissive rather than mandatory, the principle had undoubtedly been established. When the bill was established, the New York silver market was still hovering between 40 and 50 cents, and the domestic silver price was still 64.5 cents. Later, silver faction figures made extensive contacts, hoping to raise the price of silver to $1.29, and even wanted to reach a ratio of gold to silver of sixteen to one, that is, to set the price of silver at $2.08 (according to the fact that since the devaluation of the U.S. dollar in 1933, the price of gold has been $35 per ounce, so the price of silver must reach this figure to match the sixteen to one ratio). However, the U.S. Treasury Department ultimately raised the domestic silver price repeatedly to 77.57 cents. Although it is still far from the limit advocated by the silver faction figures, its implementation of the silver purchasing bill cannot be said to lack considerable sincerity. However, since the past two or three months, the Treasury Department's activities in the world silver market have clearly been less active than before, and the organization of Pittman's investigation committee is even more sufficient to demonstrate the hesitation of the silver purchasing bill. If, as Thomas said, the government has no sincerity in using silver as a genuine currency, then the principle of bimetallism in the silver bill will not be abandoned.

From our observation, the movement for bimetallism in the United States was initiated by silver faction figures, and there is no foundation for the broad interests of the entire United States in between. Using the silver production value of less than ten million U.S. dollars as the standard for the rise and fall of all values in the United States, judging from the national economy of the United States today, it is not only impossible in fact, but there is also no absolute need for it. Therefore, the so-called bimetallism movement can really be said to be a kind of delusion of silver faction figures. Moreover, in view of changes in the domestic and international situation, silver faction figures are now independently lowering the advertised silver price to $1 per ounce, hoping to finally become legal tender. There is already a trend of knowing the difficulty and retreating. When Pittman and Thomas and others set off to investigate in the future and obtain considerable results, the future of U.S. silver policy will inevitably undergo more significant changes. This can be asserted.

Thomas Asks the U.S. Treasury Department to Proceed with the Silver Purchasing Policy to Bring the Silver Price to $1.29 33

(Washington) Senator Thomas proposed a bill today asking the Treasury Department to immediately proceed with the government's silver purchasing policy. Thomas said that he would urge the government to proceed with this proposal during the next congressional term beginning on January 3 next year. This proposal calls for the continued purchase of silver until the ratio of silver to gold reaches 25:75, or until the silver price reaches $1.29. (24th Reuters Dispatch)

(Washington) The Senate today passed Thomas' proposal requiring the Treasury Department to earnestly implement the silver purchasing plan, and requiring the United States to discuss the issue of using silver as a currency standard when participating in any international monetary or stabilization conference. At the same time, McCarren's bill to abolish the silver profits tax has also been passed by the Senate as a separate bill today and sent to the House of Representatives, but it will most likely disappear invisibly in the House of Representatives, because government leaders have indicated that they will not bring it up on the floor, and even if it is brought up, it will fail. Silver faction members have also admitted that there is little hope of passage. (25th National Telegraph)

Sino-Japanese Economic Cooperation: Japanese Foreign Ministry Drafts Concrete Plan, Yokotake Ordered to Return Home to Report 34

(Tokyo) Regarding the second China policy to cope with the normalization of the North China situation, the outline of the previous Foreign Affairs and Army Council has been completed. As for economic cooperation, in order to listen to the intentions of the local area, he telegraphed and ordered Yokotake, the commercial counselor in Shanghai, to return home. He departed Shanghai on the 23rd to go east. Ambassador Jiang Zuobin is about to return home, so Foreign Minister Hirota has decided to integrate the intentions of all parties and draft a concrete plan for economic cooperation before October, implement it as soon as possible, and hand it over to Sir Ross, who is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on September 20. Therefore, the economic cooperation work of China, England, and Japan will definitely be carried out on a large scale this autumn. (25th Dentsu Dispatch)

Japan's Next Year's Budget Exceeds 2.8 Billion, Each Ministry Submits Budget Estimates, Ministry of Finance Holds Meeting for Review 37

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Finance is currently rushing to calculate the budget estimates of each ministry in order to organize them, as it must convene the first budget ministry meeting at Finance Minister Takahashi's villa in Hayama at 9:00 AM on the 26th in order to determine the iron rules for determining next year's budget. However, according to the results known as of the 24th, the number of new requests has reached 859 million yuan. There are still the 180 million yuan for the Army's Manchurian Incident expenses to be submitted at the end of this month, and the approximately 300 million yuan reserved by various ministries, which are not included. If these are added to the calculation, the total amount of new requests is still above 1.1 billion yuan. If this is combined with the base budget of 1.661 billion yuan, then the total budget for next year will exceed 2.8 billion yuan, and the difficulty of compiling the budget is actually greater than this year. Furthermore, judging from the status of the new requests submitted by various ministries, the Army accounts for 150 million yuan, the Navy accounts for 285 million yuan, and national defense expenses account for more than 50% of the new requests. Although the Ministry of Finance still hopes for the cooperation of various ministries, in reality, when compiling the budget, the question of whether it is possible to achieve a win-win situation for the military, agriculture, and finance with this huge amount of national defense expenditure is a major doubt. The total number of new requests from each ministry is listed below, with their main points separated.

Soviet Newspapers Demand Improvement of Workers' Cafeterias 40

(Moscow) According to the Soviet industrialization plan, the food distributed in the cafeterias of factories throughout the country is manufactured in large quantities by specialized factories. The number of people eating there every day is as high as 20 million, most of whom are workers. The number of people eating in factory cafeterias is therefore decreasing day by day, and the business of food factories is becoming increasingly depressed. The accumulated debts of the cafeterias amount to as much as 15 million rubles. Austria Filled with Wartime Atmosphere, Italian Army Exercises Begin, 500,000 Participants in Twenty Divisions, Eastern Africa Has Pre-Inspections and Rear Defenses 41

(Rome) The Italian people are currently attracted by the historical question of "What will England do?", and the Italian army of more than 500,000 men, led by Prime Minister Mussolini, has gathered on the Austrian border, preparing to begin major exercises tomorrow. In order to experiment with the various characteristics of new-era tactics, the simulated battles will be held in four parts: (1) north of Milan, (2) northeast of the border, (3) near Naples, and (4) near Bolzano. All Italian men who can be mobilized will be used to drill this simulated battle. Mussolini has ordered all members of the cabinet and vice ministers to participate. The main exercise will be held in Bolzano, where there are many mountains and forests, and it will be of particular interest because it will be attended by the Da Batchi aviation team. The Italian king has arrived there, and Mussolini will arrive on Sunday. This major exercise will also serve as a war exercise for attacking Abyssinia, and to silence those who say that Mussolini's power cannot protect the northern border. (25th Reuters Dispatch)

(Rome) The major army exercises have already begun. Since midnight yesterday, the atmosphere in the north has been like wartime. All cities and villages have turned off their lights, and most roads have been closed to traffic by the traffic management bureau. Army Vice Minister General Pesto Loco welcomed King Emmanuel III in the city of Trondheim yesterday morning. The diplomatic corps and military officers from England, France, Germany, Belgium, Yugoslavia, and the Soviet Union went to visit. Important figures from the Italian political world, as well as 200 members of parliament, 40 senators, and 15 ministers and vice ministers, also went to visit.

(Rome) Several of the senators are military officers. Among them, Senator Weitai Ershani, Speaker of the Senate, was originally an artillery officer. The major exercises in northern Italy are progressing rapidly after the completion of the transportation organization for the troops. Active troops and mechanized troops have now set off for the Bolzano area. At the same time, four fascist volunteer corps are also drilling in this area. At the same time, the exercises in the Sanio area have begun yesterday under the review of the Crown Prince. (25th National Telegraph)

Bolzano City. Bolzano City is located in the province of South Tyrol. In the Middle Ages, this city was originally a small fief, but was later annexed by Italy. The major army exercises are being held here, as well as in the Udine and Bergamo areas. As a result, the troops are concentrated here. The local hotels are all full. Many ministers, vice ministers, army generals, and journalists have come here to visit. It can be called a temporary boom. Prime Minister Mussolini will also visit. The theme of the major exercises is to assume that the enemy is attacking from the north, descending along the Adige and Isarco rivers, and making every effort to capture the Brenner Pass. (The border between Italy and Austria). The center of Italian resistance and the starting point for a counterattack is in the Adige River basin. There are 160,000 Italian troops, not including the troops concentrated in the vicinity. This contingent was mobilized from the provinces of Piedmont and Lombardy and the Alps near the French border. The policy of cooperation between Italy and France is being realized. The strategic position of the Italian army is based on the assumption that the enemy has already crossed the Brenner Pass and moved south to a certain point between the cities of Bolzano and Trondheim. The entire force has more than one army, and there is one division of motorized troops and several units of Alpine troops to support it. The Italian army has two armies and one division each of Alpine troops and motorized troops. King Emmanuel III is currently observing the exercises in the city of Trondheim and will not return until the end of the major exercises. (24th Havas Dispatch)

Bolzano. 500,000 troops, with infantry and cavalry complete, also have those riding in trucks, tanks, and armored vehicles. At dawn tomorrow, they will head north to fight the hypothetical enemy in the White Lena Mountain Road. At that time, it will be assumed that the enemy has invaded Italy from the German-Austrian border by forty miles, in order to test the effectiveness of mechanized troops in the Alba Mountain area. Observers believe that this move is also Italy's way of indicating that while using troops in East Africa, it is not neglecting the defense of the northern border. (24th National Er)

The British *Observer* Newspaper Discusses Mediterranean Defense, The Safety of Sea Routes to India is Worrying, Britain Should Rectify Past Mistakes 51

(London) The renowned chief writer of *The Observer*, Gavin, recently published an article saying, "Since Britain and Italy established an agreement in 1887, the British Navy's deployment of defenses in the Mediterranean has been based on Anglo-Italian friendship. This agreement was originally wise. The current situation is no longer comparable to the past, and the sea route from the Strait of Gibraltar, Malta, Egypt to Aden is the lifeline of the British Empire and must be taken into consideration. Now that Italy is hostile, it is difficult for Britain to guarantee the safety of sea routes in the Mediterranean. It is a shameful matter that the air force strength of some countries in the Mediterranean is far stronger than that of Britain. Even considering the strength of the British Navy, it is probably inferior. Britain in this area is practically being played by Italy. No wonder Italy is arrogant and overbearing. It is now impossible for us to independently safeguard the Indian route from Gibraltar to Aden. To return to bypassing the Cape of Good Hope in South Africa to reach India, in short, Britain has neglected national defense for several years, and as a result, the Abyssinian issue has arisen. If it does not use strong and powerful measures to correct past mistakes, how can it avoid danger and wash away humiliation?" (Havas, 24th)

Observations from the Paris *Temps*, Peaceful Resolution is Not Yet Hopeless 52

(Paris) The semi-official newspaper *Le Temps* published an article today stating that there is still an opportunity for a peaceful resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Although the overall situation is serious, it has not yet reached a point of hopelessness. The newspaper seems to be basing its view on the possibility that future discussions in Geneva may lead to a peaceful resolution, rather than placing much emphasis on direct exchanges of views on the diplomatic front. Many in French political circles agree with this view. *Le Temps* and *Le Débat* both advocate that Italy should seek to penetrate Abyssinia through peaceful means, as this would be more beneficial than spending huge sums on war. *Le Débat* stated that Italy should know that France and Britain, like themselves, cannot easily tolerate the destruction of the Geneva system, and that if Italy could consider the indispensability of its allies, it would be easier to abandon some of its aspirations. At the same time, both Britain and France will not make any suggestions before the League of Nations Council meeting on September 4 to make a final effort to avert war. (Reuters, 24th)

Declaration by the Second International, Demands League of Nations Sanctions Against Italy 53

Brussels. The trade union newspaper *Le Peuple* recently published a declaration by the Second International, demanding that the League of Nations impose strong sanctions on the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, and strongly advocating "blocking the Suez Canal and implementing the economic sanctions stipulated in the League of Nations Covenant so that war cannot occur." The declaration also stated that the Second International "will hold mass rallies in Charleroi on the first of next month, in Liège on the second, in Ghent and Brussels, and in Antwerp on the sixth," to protest against the attitude adopted by Italy. (Havas, 24th)

German Newspaper Defends Italy, Even Compares it to Japan 54

(Berlin) The *Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung* recently commented on the Italo-Abyssinian issue, saying, "Italy's demand to expand its colonies is perfectly reasonable. When the European War broke out, Italy joined the Allied side, and there was a secret agreement that it would assist the Allies in the war as a condition. However, after the war, when spoils were divided, Italy gained nothing. Although some rights and interests were given later, they were not enough to satisfy Italy's desires. Moreover, the country's population has increased in recent years, and the country already feels overpopulated. This is similar to the situation in Japan, and thus it has a demand to expand its colonies. However, from Germany's standpoint, if plans to redistribute colonies in Africa are to be reconsidered at this time, then Germany not only has the intention but also the right to participate in the matter. Since the Treaty of Versailles was established, Germany has been forced to remain in Central Europe, and its territory has been reduced. For the sake of national survival, it is necessary to expand its colonial bases to obtain raw materials." The newspaper also stated that when the Locarno Treaties were negotiated and when the Young Plan was negotiated in Paris, the German colonial issue was mentioned by the relevant countries. Some politicians on the Allied side also acknowledged that Germany's restoration of colonial activity was a legitimate act. Interior Minister Frick recently also stated that there are various conditions for Germany's return to the League of Nations, one of which is the return of the original colonies to Germany. The newspaper concluded by saying that Germany's demand for equal colonial rights has a strong basis. (Havas, 25th)

Roosevelt Instructs Young Party Members, Traditional Thinking Should Adapt to the Environment, Regulations Need Not Be Sacred, But Principles Are, Unite and Struggle to Break the Forces of Conservatism 55

(Washington) President Roosevelt delivered a radio address to the nation today, urging young people across the country to move forward in the new construction of the country. This address was originally addressed to the Milwaukee Young Democrats Convention. In his speech, President Roosevelt spoke of his administrative philosophy and his ideas for reforming the old order. He said, "We must make our thinking adapt to today's realities. I have one piece of advice for young people of all parties in America, namely, unity and struggle. Regulations need not be sacred, but principles are. Some of you may think that the methods of the old order are beyond the reach of young people's struggle, but this is not the case." President Roosevelt then attacked world conservatism, saying that reactionary forces often defeat progressive forces because conservatives around the world unite and hold the same old ground. Therefore, do not risk the danger of straying into many paths that lead to ruin. The old era often aimed at great wealth, but I am convinced that the new young people of America will value the abundance of life more than the overflow of wealth. In the era of George Washington, the first President of the United States, the regulations governing the relationship between blacksmith shop owners and employees could certainly no longer govern the relationship between a large company's 50,000 employees and its complex shareholders." (Reuters, 24th)

US Congress, Adjourns Until Today, Cotton and Wheat Loan Issues, Political Disputes Arise in Both Houses, Many Important Bills Passed This Session, A Valuable Page in Congressional History 56

(Washington) Congress is about to adjourn. President Roosevelt has sent a letter to Vice President Garner, expressing his deep and sincere congratulations on the achievements of the Senate, saying that a calm and fair review of the work of this Congress would be considered a historically valuable session. The Senate has now passed the House's adjournment resolution, so Congress is scheduled to adjourn tonight. (Reuters, 24th)

(Washington) After the Congressional adjournment bill was passed by the Senate today, Congress was scheduled to adjourn tonight, but the House and Senate had a fierce dispute over the third supplementary appropriation bill, so the adjournment was extended to Monday. After temporarily suspending the rule of allowing all discussions, the Senate passed two important amendments to this bill, causing Congressional leaders to find themselves in a state of great confusion. (1) Ordered the Commodity Credit Corporation to continue one-cent-per-pound loans for another year. This provision was proposed by Senator Byrnes. (2) Set the wheat loan at one and a half cents per pound. This provision was proposed by Senator Frazier. After the passage of the above two provisions, the House then approved the resolution to adjourn at midnight. However, the House refused to accept the Senate amendments, neither voting on them nor sending representatives to negotiate with the Senate, but warned the Senate that if it did not delete this provision, the bill would be shelved and die. The Senate then reconvened and asked the House to return the adjournment resolution. This was only a few minutes before the Senate's midnight adjournment. The House immediately returned the adjournment bill as requested. The Senate then decided to cancel it and did not record the vote count. Senator Robinson moved that the Senate temporarily adjourn until Monday, which was approved. The cotton loan amendment was passed without recording the vote count, and the wheat loan amendment was passed by a vote of 41 to 23. These two were an open rebellion by Southern senators against the nine-cent cotton loan announced by the authorities on Thursday. The government did not think so. Senator Byrnes said when he introduced his amendment that cotton had fallen by five dollars per bale since the nine-cent loan was announced, causing Southern cotton farmers to lose 55 million dollars, and that cotton currently under the government's one-and-two-cent loan had also lost 25 million dollars. The AAA's one-and-two-cent guarantee for cotton prices was purely illusory. If cotton farmers are forced to sell their cotton at nine cents, and the average price for the four months before January 2 is one and a half cents, then the government subsidy is only one cent, and cotton farmers actually only get one cent. The Vice President and Senators Robinson, Byrnes, and Congressman Buchanan held a meeting that lasted a long time, but

continued on page nine

Page 9

failed to resolve the deadlock. Congressman Buchanan made an impassioned speech in the House opposing the amendment, saying that it would cost tens of millions of dollars and that Congress could adjourn without dealing with this bill. After this bill was included in the amendment, it is now dead. The House cannot pass it this year. The supplementary appropriations bill is the third one proposed by this Congress, involving 95 million dollars in funding, which is intended to provide funding for the newly established Social Security Administration and the government's proposed unemployment insurance system, old-age pension system, coal bill, and neutrality bill. Buchanan said that after this bill is shelved, President Roosevelt can find other ways to finance the Social Security Administration. (Reuters, 24th)

(Washington) The Senate passed several bills tonight. The more important ones include the following three: (1) The "Wealth Redistribution Bill". The Senate voted on the issue of taxation on large amounts of property, but it did not advocate the collection of estate inheritance tax. (2) Regarding subsidies for ocean shipping, a bill was previously passed authorizing the President to cancel this subsidy within a reasonable period of time. Last night, the Senate passed a bill extending this period. (3) Regarding the bill to adjust public utilities and private companies, the House of Representatives recently passed a compromise bill and sent it to the Senate for review. It was passed by the Senate last night. In addition, the Senate also (1) approved the Treaty of Friendship between the United States and Germany and revoked the most-favored-nation clause in the treaty, (2) abolished the most-favored-nation clause in several multilateral economic agreements, (3) approved an addendum to the extradition treaty between the United States and Belgium, (4) approved the treaty between the United States and Mexico on the issue of territorial waters. Also, during the discussions in both houses today, President Roosevelt sent letters to the chairmen of the committees of both houses, requesting that they draft a bill in the fall to replace the National Industrial Recovery Act, saying, "Since the government implemented various recovery regulations in the past two years, the working class has indeed gained various benefits, but since the recovery regulations were declared unconstitutional by the Supreme Court and thus abolished, the living standards of workers have suffered a serious blow. Congress should urgently pass laws so that the benefits gained by the working class can be permanently maintained." (Havas, 20th)

Wartime Neutrality Amendment, Sent to Roosevelt for Signature, Charitable Donations for Public Utilities, Two Bills Become Law Pending Presidential Approval 57

(Washington) The Senate today passed the House's amended Neutrality Act and has now sent it to President Roosevelt for his signature. The aim of the bill is to maintain the neutrality of the United States in the event of war in Europe. (Reuters, 24th)

(Washington) The Charitable Donations Act has been sent to the White House for signature today. The original form of the bill was to increase the income tax for those with incomes above 50,000 dollars. (Washington) The Wheeler-Rayburn Public Utility Holding Company Act, after months of debate, was sent to the White House for signature today. Both houses of Congress approved a compromise solution with swift action. The House, which had previously opposed the crackdown on holding companies, first passed it by a vote of 222 to 112. The Senate, with the support of the government and the support of progressives, of course also passed it immediately. It is likely that President Roosevelt will soon sign it into law. (National Telegram, 24th)

Parisian Youths, Invent a New Navigational Aid, A Small Lighthouse Emitting Radio Waves, Can Detect Obstacles in the Dark Night and Dense Fog 58

(Paris) Pondemarice, a graduate of the École Normale Supérieure, and Henry Coudène, son of Coudène, a member of the Académie des Sciences, both young men of thirty years old, have invented a new navigational aid as a result of years of research. Once installed and adopted by ships sailing the ocean, even heavy fog or broken hulls hidden beneath the surface of the water cannot hinder navigation. Recently, one unit was installed on the giant ship "Normandie" and the test results were good. Other ships will also be installed and used. This new navigational aid is a small lighthouse installed on the front of the vessel, emitting very short radio waves rather than light rays. Ordinary light rays can only reach the places illuminated by the light rays, but the short radio waves emitted by this lighthouse can still propagate unhindered even in heavy fog or in the dark of night. If there are no obstacles ahead, these radio waves will disappear naturally. If there are obstacles ahead, the radio waves will be reflected and can be received by a second lighthouse, allowing one to detect the source of the obstacles. These two types of lighthouses, A and B, are each eight centimeters in diameter and seven and a half centimeters in depth. One emits and one receives, alternating for use, so that the location of obstacles ahead of navigation, its exact direction, and its distance, cannot escape the detection of radio waves. During the recent test of the giant ship "Normandie", the lighthouse was installed on the deck, seven kilometers from the shore. The factory chimney on land and the location of the chimney could be clearly seen, and the good results can be seen. This invention was first made by Pondé in the physics laboratory of the École Normale Supérieure, who diligently studied the effects of radio waves and obtained this result. Now, Coudène and Pondé are working together to continue to study the principles of sound and light transfer. The detection method described above is now ready, and its practical effect is not limited to one aspect. Especially in the dark sky, detecting the movement of aircraft can also be applied. This instrument emits radio waves to detect whether there are obstacles ahead, but the method used for aircraft and ships is different, and the equipment for viewing the four sides, front, back, left, and right, will naturally be more complicated. (Havas, 24th)

Japanese Military Commander Tada Hayao Arrives in Beiping 75

Tada Hayao Eloquently Discusses Sino-Japanese Amity Policies, Japan Establishes Special Service Posts in Shanxi and Suiyuan 76

Beiping Correspondence, North China Sino-Japanese Relations, Increasingly Close, After the arrival of Japanese Military Commander stationed in Tianjin, Tada Hayao, in Beiping, this morning (24th) at 9 o'clock, accompanied by his entourage and the Japanese Embassy Military Attaché Takahashi Tano, visited Wang Kemin of the Political Readjustment Council for a courtesy call after assuming office, then visited Bao Wen-yue of the Military Branch, and finally visited Yuan Liang of the Beiping Municipal Government, after which he returned to the Japanese Consulate. From 2:30 PM to 3:30 PM, he received greetings from various Chinese and foreign parties. From 5:00 PM to 6:00 PM, he held a tea party at the Japanese Embassy to entertain Chinese and foreign officials. The following is a separate account of Tada Hayao's remarks and the establishment of special service agencies by the Japanese side in North China.

Tada Hayao Discusses International Relations

Tada Hayao will return to Tianjin tomorrow (25th) and is scheduled to inspect Yuguan on the 27th. On his way back, he will review the Japanese army in Luanxian and Tangshan. Tada Hayao recently issued the following statement: "I first came to Beiping in the sixth year of the Republic of China and served as an instructor at the Army University until the ninth year before returning to my country. In the fifteenth year, I came to Beiping again, and in the sixteenth year, I returned to my country and have not come again since. In total, I lived in Beiping for six years. Now that I have come to Beiping again, passing through Zhengyangmen and the surrounding area, I see that the city gate tower is still the same, but the prosperity is not as it used to be, which is quite touching. Regarding the issue of improving Sino-Japanese diplomatic relations, although Chairman Chiang and the Chinese Central Government have repeatedly expressed their determination to adopt a pro-Japanese policy, the psychology of the people is difficult to change immediately. Therefore, Sino-Japanese relations will be difficult to fully restore to normal immediately. I sincerely hope that the people and authorities of the two countries will work hard, have patience and courage, to make the people of the two countries become compatriots, and hope that the people of the two countries treat each other with sincerity. Both sides should be able to work together, and superficial courtesies cannot achieve satisfactory results. This point is very important. Regarding the issue of Sino-Japanese economic cooperation in North China, I am not aware of the details, but from my personal observations, the lives of the people in North China are currently very difficult, and their purchasing power is very low. It is necessary to find ways to save them, and implementing economic cooperation is also a way to save them. However, whether it is politics, economy, or diplomacy, only mutual benefit for both sides can allow progress. Economic cooperation should also be based on this point. Although the cases in Hebei and Chahar have come to an end, the Japanese side hopes that your country will quickly apprehend the murderer in the Liu Zuo Zhou case, etc."

Disaster Situation in Various Counties of Henan Province – Reports from 51 Counties Including Yanshi – 77

Kaifeng Correspondence, The severity of the disaster situation in Henan Province this year is no less than that of Shandong and Hubei. However, the reports from various counties have been delayed. After repeated urging by the Provincial Disaster Relief Association, as of recently, there have been general reports from 51 counties, and the flood disaster at Guangrunpi in Anyang is particularly severe. The water depth in the Cuijiaqiao area is several feet deep. In Wenxiang, Xin'an, hailstones fell like eggs, damaging crops and destroying houses, and causing harm to people and animals. Details are not yet available. The following is a record of the disaster situation in various counties.

Yanshi On the night of July 7th, the Luoshui River overflowed the city embankment. On the 8th, the embankment broke, flooding the city. There were 274 deaths, 40,147 houses collapsed, 157,301 mu of farmland were inundated, the affected area was 900 square li, the loss was 4,337,972 yuan, 150,230 households were affected, and 60,227 people were awaiting relief.

The affected area was 260 square li, the loss was 2,626,495 yuan, 13,010 households were affected, and 70,152 people were awaiting relief.

The affected area was 1,440 square li, the loss was 400,000 yuan, and 80,000 people were awaiting relief.

Kong Lingrong Discusses The Difficulty of Blocking Yellow River Breaches The Raging Flood Must Be Diverted A Complete Blunder by Jiangsu Province in Building Dikes for Interception 78

Jinan Correspondence, Since the Yellow River breached its banks in Juancheng on July 10th, the flood has moved eastward, splitting at Wanglaohuji in Yuncheng, flowing south into Nanyang Lake and north into Dongping Lake (i.e., the Dongping low-lying depression), and then returning to the main river. Northern Jiangsu is feared to be affected by the flood. In addition to repairing the Weishan Lake dike, the Linjiaba dam has also been blocked to prevent the flood from invading south. However, due to the excessive volume of water from the breach and the strong source, the water flowing into lakes such as Nanyang, Zhaoyang, and Shushan is unable to discharge due to the obstruction of Jiangsu, resulting in widespread flooding. In recent days, not only have Tengxian and Zexian on the eastern shore of the lake breached their banks one after another, flooding the Jinpu Railway, but the Lanjia Dam has also been washed away, and water has flooded Xuzhou. Northern Jiangsu's plan to block water and prevent it from being discharged has completely failed. Recently, a water-blocking dam has been built to guard the third line of defense. The evolution of the water situation is not yet known. Kong Lingrong, Director of the Shandong Canal Engineering Bureau, recently expressed his views on the floods in Jiangsu and Shandong, arguing that the only current plan is to urgently seek diversion and discharge, and to follow the resolution of the Economic Commission's Yellow River Prevention Conference to guide the water into the sea through the proper route. The interception by Northern Jiangsu proves its misjudgment. If it continues to be insisted upon, obstructing the waterway, the disaster area in Western Shandong will expand, and Northern Jiangsu will also be swept into the flood, cutting off both the Jinpu and Longhai Railways. The Huai River diversion project will also be completely destroyed. The original text of the opinion is thousands of words long and discusses the matter in great detail. Currently, it is being revised in writing. The key points are recorded as follows.

Difficulty in Blocking Breaches At Present

After the Yellow River breaches its banks, the riverbed gradually rises, while the terrain outside the embankment is low-lying. Water flows downward, discharging for thousands of miles. The water volume from the breach accounts for nine-tenths of the total water volume, while the water in the main river is only one-tenth. Since the two major floods, there have been dramatic changes in the breach's mouth. The main current rolls eastward, and the original first, second, third, and fourth breach mouths are completely silted up, while the main river can be crossed by wading. The Yellow River carries a large amount of sediment, which is most abundant during floods, and silting is also most severe. Based on the current situation, it is feared that the current main river will be completely filled with silt, and water will be discharged from the breach mouth, resulting in a change in the river's course. Moreover, it is currently the flood season, and the rise and fall of the river water are unpredictable, and the current's momentum will also change repeatedly. The future of the breach mouth may not change its shape again. As for the breach-blocking work, progress is very slow due to the lack of funds and materials. Currently, a branch road is being laid from Lanfeng to Dongbatou, and ships are being prepared to transport supplies, which will take at least four months to complete. In addition, an diversion canal must be dug to reduce the water volume at the breach mouth before the breach-blocking work can begin. Currently, only work such as transporting materials, digging diversion canals, blocking dry breaches, and making wrapping heads can be done.

Jiangsu's Misjudgment in Obstructing Water

According to current measurements, the water from the breach is 54 meters higher than sea level (taking the Jianghuai sea outlet as the base point). Measurements ten days ago showed that the water level of the Shanhu Lake was 20 meters lower than the water from the breach. With the rising water level in recent days, the water level should also be 18 meters lower than the water from the breach. This proves that Jiangsu's dike construction is a complete misjudgment. The dike must be raised by another 18 meters to prevent the breach water from invading south. However, this is not possible in reality, because if the dike is raised further, Northern Jiangsu's abundance will be flooded, and the isolated dry land of Shanxian and Chengwu in Western Shandong will also be submerged in water. As for the water level at the Hanzhuang Sluice Gate, it has now reached 36.3 meters. During the major flood fifteen years ago, the water level was 36.5 meters. Comparing the two, the difference is only slightly over 1 decimeter. With such a strong water force, it is inevitable that the Lanjia Dam and the Hanzhuang Sluice Gate will be washed away. Currently, the flood water rushes out from the breach, with a flow rate of 5,000 cubic meters per second, flowing into the disaster area. The momentum has stabilized somewhat, and the flow rate is approximately 2,600 cubic meters per second. With such a large volume of water and such a high flow rate, it will inevitably flood if it cannot be properly diverted and discharged. Jiangsu does not know how to guide the water into the sea, but only knows how to block it. The unprecedented flood disaster in Northern Jiangsu has already proven that its previous policies were a complete failure.

Divert and Discharge Should Be Planned

To fundamentally reduce the flood disasters in Jiangsu and Shandong, the only solution is to block the breach, but blocking the breach is currently impossible. The current priority should be to quickly study the method of official diversion and discharge. There are approximately several solutions: (1) Dig the Linjiaba dam to divert water into the Bulao River, reinforce the southern embankment of the Bulao River, enter the Central Canal from the Bulao River, reinforce the eastern embankment of the canal, and build an outer embankment on the Central Canal below Qutangji, and then discharge it into the sea through the Liutang River. Its capacity can discharge approximately 1,000 cubic meters per second. Divert water into the Central Canal from the Hanzhuang Lake outlet gate and also discharge it into the sea through Liutang, which can discharge approximately 600 cubic meters per second. (2) The northern flow of the breach water can be discharged into the Yellow River through the Jishui flood plains of Pingyi, with a capacity of 400 cubic meters per second. It can be discharged into the Yellow River through the Songjin River, with a capacity of 600 cubic meters per second. In summary, the amount of water discharged from the north and south routes above is 2,600 cubic meters per second, which is not much different from the flow rate of the breach water, and the water situation should no longer flood. (3) Starting from the old course of the Yellow River in Fengxian County, build a north-south large dike of approximately 300 li in length to prevent the Yellow River water from flooding westward. (4) Leave several outlets in the old course of the Yellow River north of Xuzhou and create wrapping heads, which can also absorb a portion of the water and reduce the flooded area in Xuzhou and Huai'an.

Wuxi Severe Punishment for Illegally Raising Seed Prices 80

Zhang Zhaozhen, the manager of the Dadong Hotel on the road, was found to have privately established an organization to sell substandard silkworm seeds and raise seed prices. After investigation by the Supervision Department of the Public Security Bureau, Zhang Zhaozhen, Zhang Gu's, Wang Shenglin, Zheng Jianshu, and others were arrested and transferred to the County Government for interrogation and detention. Meanwhile, the County Magistrate reported the situation to the Department of Construction and requested instructions. It is reported that the Department of Construction severely punished them in accordance with the Jiangsu Provincial Silkworm Seed Control Regulations, imposing a fine of ten times the amount (approximately over 20,000 yuan) to prevent other seed vendors from raising seed prices again.

Request to Investigate and Prohibit Private Sales of Copper Coins 81

Recently, the market price of copper coins in the town has plummeted. At the highest, each yuan reached around 3,600 cash, causing significant harm to merchants. The reason for the sharp decline is that some people are privately selling large quantities of copper coins from counties such as Yixing and Liyang to Wuxi because each yuan can be exchanged for around 3,700 cash there. Xu Ruzhou, a standing committee member of the town's Liquor and Sauce Shop Association, and Shi Qinglin, a standing committee member of the Tobacco Exchange Association, submitted a petition to the County Government yesterday, requesting that it issue a strict prohibition and investigation of private sales to maintain business.

(4) Zhang Xingzhen, a young woman from No. 114 Zhugan Lane, committed suicide by swallowing opium due to a domestic quarrel. (5) Mrs. Liu, wife of Fang Amao of No. 3 Chenghuang Arch, committed suicide by swallowing acid after arguing with her husband. All of the above five cases were treated at the Municipal Hospital and were able to recover. (6) A vendor named Ni at the Zhakou Railway Station committed suicide due to living difficulties. The Mountain Court examined the body and provided a coffin for burial.

Baker Aircraft's Inspection Opinions

The chairman then reported on the inspection of disaster conditions in the provinces of Henan, Shandong, Hebei along the Yellow River. (Details were already seen in yesterday's interview with Mr. Xu.) He also released the opinion of Consultant Baker to Vice President Xu, after flying over the disaster area of the Yellow River and Yangtze River. The original text is as follows: From the 15th to 17th of this month, I accompanied engineers from the National Economic Council and others, aboard [unidentified] aircraft, to survey the disaster areas. I will now describe what I saw and the opinions I gathered: (1) Shandong: Flying along the railway from Jinan to Jining, northward to the intersection of the Grand Canal and the Yellow River, then along the Yellow River to view the breaches, and then turning eastward back to Jining, forming a triangle. Along the route, there was very little flooding east of the Grand Canal. Some [unidentified] lake land, which could be cultivated when the water was shallow, is now submerged, but the area is not extensive. West of the Grand Canal, within the triangle traversed by the plane, is a vast expanse of water, estimated to be 2,800 square miles. Excluding the various lakes, both large and small, and the higher ground that has not been submerged, there are still 2,000 square miles under water. However, in many areas, the water is only a few feet deep, and in some places, the land has already emerged. If no further flooding occurs, cultivation will be possible in half a month. Two-thirds of the current flow of the Yellow River is diverted through the breach into the triangle, and then back into the Yellow River itself via the Grand Canal. Therefore, a total of 95% of the Yellow River's flow still follows its original course, with only a small portion diverted into the Grand Canal. Near the breach in the Yellow River dyke, the river mud has accumulated, burying villages, with only the rooftops visible. It is estimated that in the future, the ground within one or two miles of the breach will be elevated by two or three feet due to the accumulation of silt. The remaining submerged land will also be raised by several inches. Whether this silt is beneficial or harmful to agriculture cannot be determined without experimentation. When the plane passed over Jinan, the number of refugees seen in the straw sheds along the railway was not large, suggesting that most refugees have already left for other places or returned to their homes. The dyke built by the Jiangsu provincial authorities at Huishan Lake, which successfully prevented the Yellow River from overflowing into Jiangsu, is noteworthy. (2) Poyang Lake: On the 16th, [unidentified] circled Poyang Lake. The eastern part of the lake is mostly high ground, and except for a small portion along the shore, there are no signs of disaster. The western and southern parts of the lake are mostly marshes and shallows, which can be cultivated for spring crops, or in dry years, for autumn crops. However, as this land is inherently part of the lake, it is naturally intended to accommodate excess lake water and has no dykes for defense. Therefore, the current flooding cannot be considered a disaster. (3) The low-lying and滩地 along the Jinghan Railway and the Yangtze River are all submerged, but this cannot be considered a disaster, as this type of submerged land [unidentified] can be cultivated for spring crops and is typically submerged by the river water during the summer floods. The Yangtze River dykes are all behind this type of land and are intact, except for one place in Anhui. The breach in the dyke in Anhui was built after the 1931 flood. The inner dyke was breached, and the reclaimed lake will [unidentified] revert to its former state. (4) Han River dyke Sai He: On the afternoon of the 16th, [unidentified] water [unidentified] surveyed along the Han [unidentified]. Northwest of Hankou, there is a low-lying area that originally produced [unidentified] weeds, used for making baskets and mats. Now, it is a large lake. When the water from the Dong River recedes, the water there will naturally flow out. West and south of [unidentified] Han, there are large tracts of land, [unidentified] a collection of many low-lying areas. As usual, this type of low-lying area is filled with water during this time of year. Now, the fields along the edges of each low-lying area are also submerged. However, this situation is common during periods of extremely high water levels and is not unusual. The current water level of the Yangtze River at Hankou is around 43.8 feet. After the unusual [unidentified] period, and as the water continues to recede northward, the water in the aforementioned low-lying areas will also naturally recede. Furthermore, the people who cultivate this type of land can be called [unidentified] reclaiming people. Because this type of land is not privately owned and is necessary for regulating the river's capacity, it is highly questionable whether the government and society have a responsibility to provide relief to these encroaching people. If the government does have a responsibility, it seems to fall on the provincial government, not the central government. Flying further north, the two major breaches in the Nang River were seen. The river water rushed into the dyke, spreading rapidly, so the water on the ground was only a few inches deep. The submerged area is smaller than when the flood first came. Some of the land has emerged, and farmers have begun to cultivate it. The accompanying engineers said that the sediment deposited by the breaches contains a lot of sand, which is harmful to the soil. Some of the land needs to wait until the water from the breaches stops flowing before it can be cultivated. Many farmers have already returned to their fields. In total, in western Hubei, excluding the lakes and swamps that are inherently uncultivable, the area currently submerged does not exceed 600 square miles. (5) On the 17th, flew around Dongting Lake and along the Yangtze River to Yichang. The situation in Dongting Lake is similar to that in Poyang Lake. The eastern part of Dongting Lake is higher in elevation, and only the fields along the shore have been submerged at some point or are still submerged, with no signs of disaster. The land on the west and south sides of the lake is formed by lake sediment, with a wide area and extremely humid conditions, where lotus roots and reeds are grown. Now, it is a sheet of water, indistinguishable from the lake. Some of it could have been planted with rice during extremely dry periods, and some dry rice has been planted, but it has also been submerged. Although this type of land is surrounded by dykes, the engineering is not strong. The water level of the lake this time is not much higher than usual, and there is no impact from floods, but all the dykes have collapsed. It can be seen that the engineering is careless. Some believe that the mud carried by the lake water, after the water recedes, will remain on the ground, increasing the productivity of the land. Farmers benefit from the silt, so they build dykes along the lake shore with the intention of merely going through the motions. If so, then the people in that area seem to have no need for relief. Along the Yangtze River from Shashi to Songzi, the submerged land on both banks has now completely emerged, and cultivation has begun. The residents who live by the water may have needed aid at the beginning of the flood, but now they are able to use their own resources and abilities to engage in work. In total, the area of fields in western Hunan that are still under water does not exceed 600 square miles. (6) Conclusion: From the above observations, only a portion of the area along the Xiang River in Hubei Province needs urgent relief. In other disaster areas, disaster victims can be assisted by establishing credit cooperatives to implement agricultural assistance. After engineers have drafted plans for building and repairing dykes, disaster victims can also be recruited to rebuild houses. They should be [unidentified] to raise the ridge of their houses. During this flood, except for those very close to the breaches, the foundations of houses [unidentified] high could be preserved intact. As for the relief in Hunan Province, the province's efforts are sufficient, and the province's relief agencies can handle it independently. The province should pay special attention to the grain storage system. Grain stored in good years can be used to regulate the needs of bad years. The surplus of one county can supplement the deficiency of Zheng. Even within a county, the land varies in elevation, and there are different fortunes depending on drought or continuous rain. If more warehouses can be set up, they can effectively regulate the supply. The situation in Poyang Lake seems to require no attention. What should be paid most attention to now is the situation within the triangle of the Yellow River and the Grand Canal in Shandong Province. The Shandong Provincial Government has moved disaster victims out for food. Now, in the autumn harvest season, disaster victims should be summoned back to rebuild their homes. What is needed is agricultural assistance. After engineers have drafted plans for repairing dykes, the strong men among the disaster victims can work on the dykes and be given appropriate compensation to support themselves and their families. Farmers who rebuild houses should also be encouraged to raise the foundations, so that in the future, even if they encounter floods, if they are not in the path of the rapid flow from the breach, they can be preserved after the water recedes. The conclusion drawn from this trip is that the current method of preventing floods is still to focus on strengthening and raising the dykes. The government needs to have an improved organization and equipment to engage in this, not only to maintain the dykes in peacetime, but also to be able to cope with emergencies. Fortunately, the Yangtze River dykes were able to resist the flood, demonstrating the flood control effectiveness of [unidentified] construction. The dykes at the breach of [unidentified] River were not built by the National Flood Relief Association after the 1931 flood. The cause of the Yellow River breach is not difficult to investigate. The reason is the negligence of the dyke work. However, no matter how strong a dyke is, it can still be breached under extraordinary circumstances. Therefore, there should also be plans for how to cope with breaches in peacetime. Such as this time the breach of Xiang River, or may think that is not any dyke body can support, therefore on one hand should have [unidentified] effectiveness emergency relief organization, on the other hand should have improved [unidentified] dyke organization, and [unidentified] the opportunity of flood and the need of relief, [unidentified] can be reduced.

Saving Disaster Victims is Saving Lives: Donate One More Penny, Save One More Life

Joint Sino-Foreign Survey Report on the Disaster

Mr. Xu further reported on the report by Zhang Qichun, chief engineer of the China International Famine Relief Commission, and others, after inspecting the Shandong flood area. The inspection lasted a total of nine days, starting from Jining and returning to Jining on the 16th. Most of the journey was through rural areas, with only the cities of Jiaxiang and Juye. Upstream from Yansikou, the journey stopped due to sediment accumulation that made further progress impossible. In terms of population, the rural areas are more densely populated than the cities. Standing on the bow of the boat, with a telescope, more than thirty villages can be surveyed per hour. During this nine-day trip, only two places were seen that were not under water: one was a part of [unidentified] village, exposed above the water by less than two feet, and the other was a large mound with a small temple on it. During the first 24 hours, the only living things seen were one cow, one horse, and four sheep, standing on a mound. Most of the local houses are built of mud [unidentified], and have sunk [unidentified], so nine out of ten are [unidentified]. The number of uninhabited villages [unidentified] can be calculated. No less than 6,000 villages have been submerged. Jining has already moved 66,891 [unidentified] refugees out of the area, and more than 20,000 people are waiting for trains to move out. There are 15,000 disaster victims in Jiaxiang and 5,000 in Juye. The authorities are working hard on relief efforts, but the increasing depth of the water makes it very difficult to transport food to the more remote villages and to rescue the disaster victims to Jining. Only one village has one week's worth of food left. In some places, efforts are being made to rescue the elderly and young children under 50 and under 15 years old first. Some disaster victims who spoke to me have expressed despair because they have no food or boats and have no way to escape. According to the postal map, the population in the disaster area is the densest in Shandong Province. If the average population of the province is 500 people per square mile, then the original population in the disaster area must be more than 700 people per square mile. Each household cultivates only 20 to 30 mu of land. It is rare to find someone who has more than 50 mu of land. The density of villages is probably the highest in the country, and the number of victims can be imagined. I met a village where nine out of ten houses had been destroyed. How can we [unidentified] send food to the many compatriots who are still struggling in the water if we cannot navigate a small boat on the [unidentified] deep water surface, to those villages that originally had 4,000 households? It is not easy for Jining, with its local resources, to supply 600 bags of flour per day to the gathering disaster victims. Therefore, the disaster victims must be moved out to other counties [unidentified]. The most needed thing now is urgent relief funds. The number of disaster victims being housed in Jining and other counties is increasing, and fuel and food [unidentified] are becoming increasingly scarce. The future is long, so what will happen in the months to come? Therefore, raising funds for urgent relief is the most important plan at present. As for repairing the dykes, it needs to wait until the water recedes. There are currently 119 shelters in the affected counties, and the winter clothing of disaster victims has no boat. There are also some places where the water is very shallow, so even if there are boats, they cannot travel. And the silt under the water is deep [unidentified], so even wading is impossible. Many disaster victims can only sit and wait for death. In some high places, there are still sorghum ears showing above the water, which are the only remaining possessions. But because they are few in number, they are even more precious. The disaster victims float the vat of water on the surface, tie one end of the rope [unidentified] to the body, or swim or wade, and risk collecting the treasure that has been left behind, and let the women and children flee for the lives of their people, which is praiseworthy. In one village [unidentified] there are two households whose water is five feet deep, and still heard the sounds of children crying and dogs barking [unidentified], because their occupants are still guard its wooden beams doors and windows, and other possessions. Baker's Proposal: Consult on Solutions

There is also a letter from Consultant Baker to Vice President Xu, proposing to convene a joint meeting of Yellow River water conservancy engineers and relief personnel to discuss a unified approach to engineering and relief work. Briefly, it says, "Attached is a translated report from Zhang Qichun and [unidentified] Lian Kailan after their inspection of the Shandong disaster area. According to the report, there are more than one million disaster victims in the 3,000 square miles, but because the water is shallow and the mud is deep, boats and vehicles are useless and food cannot be transported, so there is a risk of sitting and waiting for death. You must also be well aware of this situation from your inspection. I understand that the water conservancy agencies are planning engineering projects in the area. From the perspective of engineers, they naturally focus on the technology and economics of the project, and disaster relief is not their responsibility, so it will inevitably be beyond the scope of their plans. But in reality, engineering plans have a great impact on relief methods and costs. Therefore, I propose to convene a joint meeting of relevant engineering and relief personnel to discuss the plans together. The participants should include: (1) key personnel and senior engineers from the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission; (2) representatives from the Shandong Provincial Relief Association, and representatives from this association. In addition, Mr. Zhang and Mr. Kai [unidentified] should also be invited to join because they are very familiar with the situation in the disaster area. Mr. Zhang is the acting chief engineer of the China International Famine Relief Commission, and Mr. Kailan is the former [unidentified] director of the China International Famine Relief Commission and is currently the accountant. The purpose of the meeting is to coordinate the work of engineering and relief in Shandong to make them mutually supportive. How to transport food in the area should also be a matter of common discussion. If you consider this proposal to be good, please convene the meeting as soon as possible."

Li and Others Launch a Donation Drive

A letter signed by Li Yingsheng and others was sent to the Flood Relief Association yesterday, stating, "Dear Sirs, we have learned that the Yangtze River provinces have suffered a terrible flood this year, and the loss of lives, livestock, and property is incalculable. It is truly an unprecedented disaster. We are grateful to the gentlemen of your association for your public spirit and righteousness in advocating for the disaster victims and raising funds for disaster relief and local reconstruction. After reading the newspapers, we are very impressed. However, in this time of global economic recession, and with Shanghai's economy becoming increasingly strained, we are deeply concerned that people in society may find it difficult to donate cash, and may feel willing but unable to do so. We propose that your association launch a campaign to allow people to donate goods for relief. For example, our friend Mr. Chen is willing to donate one of his two radios. Mr. Guan Xinxin has an old car and is also willing to donate it. Mr. Huang Xiangchen has dozens of pieces of furniture and other items that a friend did not claim and is also willing to donate them. We believe that if this is done, people who have surplus items or clothing will also be happy to support it. Because friends are reluctant to sell their items for fear of losing face or because they are afraid that pawnshops will offer low prices. If your association does this, it can be quite significant. The collected items should be listed and advertised in the newspaper on a regular basis, and auctions should be held, with the highest bidder winning. People from all walks of life can participate in the bidding, but it is advisable to auction the items separately to avoid the disadvantages of being [unidentified] interrupted. The above benefits both the donors and the recipients. Whether it is feasible, we await your [unidentified] decision. We are doing this for the benefit of the public. Cash donations are also welcome, but there should also be a way to donate goods for relief. If you can donate silver, it would be even better. Li Yingsheng, Ren Daren, Zhou Junjie, Lai Gang."

Distributing Medicines in Disaster Areas

This year's floods have caused disasters everywhere. In addition to the deaths of more than 200,000 people, with corpses floating and sinking, which cannot be fully salvaged, the loss of houses and the submerging of fields, those climbing trees and rooftops, exposed to the scorching sun and steamed by the turbid currents, have led to widespread epidemics, spreading rapidly, and countless people have succumbed to illness and death. The Shanghai Association for Raising Funds for Flood Relief in Various Provinces has distributed emergency medicines, including 2,000 bottles each of cholera medicine and cholera powder to Shandong Province, 400 packets each of Wan Jin You, Rendan, and Liang Dan, 2,000 packets of Wu Shi Cha, 1,600 bottles of five types of medicine in total, including Fo Dan, Jisheng Dan, Jiuji Dan, Lei Ji San, and Er Tian You, to Shandong Province; a total of 1,200 bottles of cholera medicine and dysentery powder to Hebei Province; A total of 800 packets of Wu Shi Cha, Ren Dan, and Liang Dan, A total of 1,000 bottles of six types of medicine to Hebei Province: Lei Ji San, Jiuji Dan, Wan Jin You, Fo Dan, Jisheng Dan, Er Tian You, a total of 1,000 bottles A total of 2,200 packets of cholera medicine, dysentery powder, Wu Shi Cha, Ren Dan, Liang Dan, Malaria Pills a total of three types of medicine to Henan Province: A total of 3,500 bottles six types of medicine of Wan Jin You, Er Tian You, Fo Dan, Lei Ji San, Jisheng Dan, dysentery powder to Henan Province: A total of 6,000packets of Wu Shi Cha, Malaria Pills Wan Jin You, Lei Ji San, a total of 800 bottles A total of 3,500 bottles of cholera medicine, dysentery powder, , A total of 5,200packets of Wu Shi Cha, Malaria Pills A total of 3,150 bottles of of Wan Jin You, Er Tian You, Fo Dan, Jisheng Dan, Ren Dan, Liang Dan, Lei Ji San,, 1,100 bottles of cholera medicine, Jisheng Dan, Malaria Pills to Hubei Province a A total of 7,000 bottles cholera medicine, 8,400 bottles Malaria Pills to outside party and government organizations and public charity organizations, A total of 1,000 packets Wu Shi Cha,, A total of 7,400 bottles Wan Jin You, Er Dan, Fo Dan, Jisheng Dan,人丹，良丹，雷擊散 to . However, the disaster victims numbered in the tens of millions, densely packed together, and the epidemic [unidentified] series [unidentified], medicine [unidentified] not enough to treat even one in ten thousand. We rely on the major pharmacies and national [unidentified] brands to provide a continuous supply of various epidemic medicines to help the poor and sick survive. As the Buddha said, "Saving a life is better than building a seven-story pagoda." Saving a life early can save countless more lives.

Ambassador Chiang Yesterday Departed for Japan to Resume Post; Scheduled to Return to China Again Before the Sixth Plenary Session 86

Our country's ambassador to Japan, Chiang Tso-pin, departed yesterday afternoon at 6:30 PM from Shanghai, accompanied by Second Secretary of the Embassy, Yang Hsueh-lun, aboard the Chang Hing Shipping Company's "Empress of Russia" steamer, to return to his post in Japan. He plans to return to China again before September 20th to attend the Sixth Plenary Session. Yesterday morning, Ambassador Chiang visited the President of the Legislative Yuan, Sun Ke, and attended a farewell banquet hosted by Mayor Wu and others. Details of these events are recorded as follows:

Separate Farewells

Yesterday morning at 9:30 AM, Ambassador Chiang, accompanied by Secretary Yang Hsueh-lun, drove to visit Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke for a lengthy conversation. Besides exchanging views, Chiang also bid farewell to Sun. Subsequently, he dispatched Secretary Yang to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to bid farewell to Tang Yu-jen, who had arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing that morning, specifically representing Acting Foreign Minister Wang to bid farewell to Ambassador Chiang. Around 11:00 AM, Chiang returned to the International Hotel to handle private matters and receive relatives and friends.

Mayor's Farewell Banquet

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tieh-cheng hosted a farewell banquet for Ambassador Chiang at his private residence in Hai-ge yesterday afternoon. Chiang, accompanied by Secretary Yang, arrived for the banquet around 12:00 PM. Guests included Minister to France Gu Weijun, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Yu Ming, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government Yu Hongjun, and various bureau chiefs. The banquet concluded merrily around 2:00 PM. Former Minister to Switzerland Wu Kaisheng also held a tea party at the International Hotel yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM to bid farewell to Chiang. Attendees included Mayor Wu Tieh-cheng, Minister to France Gu Weijun, Central Committee member Wang Zhengting, Director of the Foreign Affairs Office Yu Ming, Wang Xiaolai, Chen Guangfu, Fan Guang, Liu Yunfang, Wang Changchun, Wang Dasui, and dozens of others. The gathering dispersed at 5:30 PM, after which Chiang immediately departed by car to the Gonghexiang Wharf to board the ship and set sail for Japan to resume his post.

Yesterday's Return to Post

Ambassador Chiang's recent leave to return to China included audiences with Chairman Chiang and President Wang to report on the situation in Japan. Now that his leave has expired, he is setting off to resume his post, planning to return before the Sixth Plenary Session. Therefore, his wife and family did not accompany him yesterday. The "Empress of Russia" set sail at 6:30 PM yesterday afternoon. Ambassador Chiang arrived at the Gonghexiang Wharf at 6:00 PM to board the ship. Representatives from various Chinese and foreign circles were present to see him off, including Commissioner Wang Changchun, representing Mayor Wu and the Municipal Government, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Yu Ming, Section Chief Zhao Tiezhang, Director Cai of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Inspector-General Zhu Dasui representing Director Cai, Liu Yunfang representing Central Committee member Wang Zhengting, former Minister to Switzerland Wu Kaisheng, Chairman of the Municipal Council Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Cotton Industry Control Committee Chen Guangfu, Guo Bingwen, Xia Qifeng, Fan Guang, Zhao Jinqing, and Ambassador Chiang's daughters, totaling dozens of people. Japanese Ambassador to China Akira Ariyoshi also attended with Counselor Areno, Secretary Yokokawa, and Japanese Consul-General Ishisha to bid farewell. Security was tight around Gonghexiang Wharf. After arriving, Ambassador Chiang shook hands with each of the well-wishers to express his gratitude.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Actively Engages in Anti-Smoking Campaign; Jointly Expands Public Awareness with Various Sectors; Registration of Persuasion Teams Nears Completion; Movie Theaters Add Anti-Smoking Slides 87

Since the establishment of the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has been actively carrying out anti-smoking campaigns in the city. In order to eliminate smokers within a limited time, it has joined forces with various agencies and organizations to hold large-scale public awareness campaigns regularly. The details are as follows:

Door-to-Door Persuasion

The Municipal Public Security Bureau, in order to investigate the number of smokers and persuade them to register for quitting smoking, has issued a circular to all branch bureaus and district offices, organizing persuasion teams to mobilize fully in mid-month to carry out persuasion. The harm of opium, its damage to the body, its economic costs, and the various theft behaviors of smokers are explained at any time, and smokers are kindly advised to register and quit. As a result, the number of smokers voluntarily registering has been more enthusiastic than before. This persuasion work will come to an end at the end of this month.

Expanding Public Awareness

The bureau, in order to limit and eliminate smokers and carry out widespread public awareness to achieve significant results in the anti-smoking effort, has specially collaborated with the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Health Bureau, the Education Bureau, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, the Citizens' Federation, the Women's Association, the Municipal Farmers' Association, and other agencies and organizations to hold expanded public awareness campaigns. Preparations have already begun and are scheduled to be held next month.

Movie Ticket Slogans

Anti-smoking movie publicity has been agreed upon by various movie theaters after the bureau sent personnel to each of them. Therefore, as soon as the film is made, it can be screened. In addition, anti-smoking slogans have been drafted and will be posted on various main roads on the first of next month for citizens to read.
