Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 146

— (Yinhu)

We see a person who does a good job in a career must go through decades of experience to develop. The reason for this development must come from accumulated experience and long-term practice. Now politicians are often transferred every few months. It is of course difficult to harvest good results.

Human feelings are as thin as autumn clouds. This is a sentence to describe the fickleness of the world; in fact, human feelings must be much thinner than autumn clouds.

Now people's feelings are the most unpredictable. The clouds in summer change more than the clouds at any other time. Human feelings are as illusory as summer clouds. But it is a very good metaphor.

Now, no matter what you do, you have to talk about qualifications. In fact, people with qualifications do not necessarily have talents, and people with talents, if they do not have experience; the things they do still have to wait until they have experience before they can do well.

Ji Mulang 147

— Tiansheweng

This was probably in the summer of a certain year. At this time, I and a few friends were taking refuge from the heat in the ×× Academy outside Beiguo, reading books and playing chess in the painting room. At night, a few friends rowed a small boat and rippled in the lake. I only saw high mountains and small moons, and countless stars dotted the lake. The clear breeze was gentle and the coolness was pleasant. There were friends who played the flute and sang loudly. This scene and this feeling are still vivid in my mind. Where can I get it back now!

I remember one evening, the new rain had just cleared, and the mountain colors were like a beauty after bathing. There were especially many people catching fish and shrimp by the lake. We also took fishing rods and fished under Shiguting. Suddenly, I saw a young man in a large-sleeved cloth coat, holding an umbrella in his hand, walking slowly across the bridge. After passing Shiguting, he went straight to Pujisi Temple. It turned out that the academy where we were taking refuge from the heat was next to Pujisi Temple. There was a monk in the temple who could write a few poems, write in the style of Wang Xizhi, and understood some Shaolin boxing. He often came to chat with us. At this time, we saw the young man walking into the temple and couldn't help but feel a little rare.

Later, through the monk's introduction, we learned that the young man's surname was Mu, his name was Yaoshu, and he called himself Mulang. He was a high-achieving student at Shanghai Nanyang Public School. We expressed our admiration to him, and he stammered and seemed awkward in speech. He had a very solid foundation in Chinese studies, and his English was also excellent. He could also perform a few sets of Neijiaquan. But his appearance was very simple and mature for his age, and he seemed a bit like a country bumpkin. Who knew he was a university student?

The summer vacation was over, and we all went to school. We said goodbye to Mulang for a few months and didn't meet each other. However, we often had letters back and forth. The year after we graduated, we received Mulang's wedding invitation. We invited a few friends to his house for a wedding feast. At this time, the congratulatory guests filled the door. There were students in suits, bald monks, and remnants of the imperial examination era. The scene was bizarre and very interesting. In our hometown custom, on the night of the wedding, the bride and groom sit side by side and drink with the congratulatory guests, which is called "Helang." Mulang had a whimsical idea and actually pulled a few monks to贺郞, and made "Monks贺郞" the topic of the drinking game, forcing the congratulatory guests to write a poem and the bride to pour the wine. This can be called a unique贺郞. The now famous Taixu Monk was one of the 贺 guests at the time.

A few years later, one day, I accidentally read a newspaper and suddenly saw the news that Mulang had been shot by a warlord in Sichuan. I was really shocked. It turned out that after graduating from Nanyang Public School, Mulang had worked as the principal of a girls' school in Chengdu. According to the accusations announced by a certain warlord, Mulang and a certain female student committed adultery in the classroom during the day. Therefore, he was shot alive.

This was probably ten years ago? I still think about him now!

Small Pebbles 148

— Yan Boguang

According to a friend, "Small pebbles were not very useful in the past. Since the popularity of cement buildings, small pebbles have become necessities." Therefore, his early stone mountain, which was equivalent to waste, is now actually willing to pay a high price to sign a contract and organize a large-scale stone mining company to make profits from it. This may be something he never dreamed of?

One day, a friend very sincerely told me an anecdote about small pebbles in his childhood. He said, "In my youth, because I couldn't hold back the flames of youth, I was looking for a partner everywhere. After a few months, I fell in sweet love with Na, but Na's family was very stubborn and did not allow me to cross the Min gate. As the saying goes, the more severe the oppression, the stronger the reactionary explosion. One day I was wandering under the window of her back building, no, I was wandering more than once. This day can be regarded as a lucky day. I was looking up at the window when suddenly, with a 'ya' sound, the window opened. Seeing the opportunity, I immediately took out the love letter I had written in advance and hidden in my pocket and wanted to pass it to her. She put down a silk thread and hung the letter up. After that, as long as I picked up a small pebble on the ground and threw it at the tile, she would open the window. In this way, after a year of back and forth, the two achieved the purpose of marriage by all means. At that time, a friend sent a pair of wedding couplets with the embedded sentence 'stone marriage'."

Now he often praises the pebbles in front of his friends as his heroes. Four words can represent the completion of the marriage. "Throwing a brick to attract jade." His wife's name has the word "jade."

High-Interest Loans 150

— Zhu Ying

My friend has a neighbor who makes a living by lending money at high interest rates. There are three types of lending he does. The first type is loans above ten yuan (usually up to twenty yuan), with an interest rate of one dime per yuan per month. When borrowing, for a ten-yuan loan, only nine yuan is given, deducting one month's interest in advance, but the IOU must be written for twenty yuan in order to avoid losses in principal and interest in case of litigation. The second type is loans around five yuan, starting with a booklet, collecting one yuan per month including principal and interest. After collecting for ten months, the booklet will be cancelled as full payment of principal and interest. The third type is accounts of one or two yuan, also with booklets. For example, if you borrow one yuan from him, you have to pay ten copper coins in interest every day at a certain time when he comes. Then he will stamp a small seal on the booklet as proof that the interest for that day has been collected.

Those who borrow the first type are mostly small clerks in long gowns who borrow from him because they are in dire straits with gambling. The customers of the second and third types are almost entirely ignorant women and vendors. He actually employs four runners. For every yuan lent out, the runner gets a dime commission. At the same time, he also has several brothers who act as thugs for him. If someone defaults on the debt or delays in paying interest, these brothers will give them a good beating. Fortunately, after the beating, he does not worry about the beaten person selling his wife and children to pay off the debt and treat guests. (The jargon is called "pulling the table.")

This high-interest lender is said to have been very poor three years ago. Later, he borrowed one hundred yuan at an interest rate of five cents per yuan per month, mixed for three years, and now not only has he paid off the one hundred yuan, he can actually collect one hundred and twenty or thirty yuan in interest every month. He gets up early every morning and is busy going out to collect interest, and does not return home until three or four in the afternoon. He said that in another nine or six years, he will not have to do this business anymore. But even now, his wife is already wearing a diamond ring on her finger.

Little Western Paradise 151

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: The Qi Faction Clambers High to Flatter, Reprimanding Petty Officials; Female Authority Roars, Annoying the Mistress

So, his face broke into a smile as he said: "The person who was just speaking to me is Qiu Zecheng, the Chief Secretary of Commissioner Lan. He is my elder sister's husband, and as close to me as my own brother. Precisely because of that, he tends to act like an elder brother with a lot of airs. If I were at home, I wouldn't put up with that. But now I need him to get me a letter of recommendation from Commissioner Lan, so there's no choice but to take his orders." "Jia Duocai! I heard you say that Commissioner Lan is a relative of yours. So now, the Chief Secretary is your relative too?" Zhang Jiefu blushed and said, "Perhaps Mr. Jia didn't hear clearly. I said from the beginning that the Chief Secretary is a relative." Jia Duocai laughed and said, "No matter what, you're still better off than me. Look, I've ended up with two refugees from the Gansu famine as relatives." As they spoke, they approached the doorway of Jia Duocai's room. Miss Yue was also secretly peering through a crack in the door, wanting to see the excitement of welcoming the high-ranking central officials. Hearing Jia Duocai's words, especially in front of so many people, she felt truly uncomfortable, and her face immediately turned pale. Fortunately, she was hidden behind the curtain and wasn't seen by Jia Duocai. Zhang Jiefu also had other things on his mind. He didn't pay much attention to Jia Duocai's words. He returned to his room, closed the door, ground ink, spread out paper, and wrote a letter in semi-cursive script. He then took the letter he had written in regular script the previous night and sealed them together in a large official envelope. (299)

Records of Lingering Fragrance 152

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

As chance would have it, four or five years prior, when my entire family was living in Paris, my mother and several of her elderly friends had experimented with Western hair dyes, and I was determined to introduce them to the Empress Dowager. At that time, I was truly enthusiastic, not even considering that if the hair dye I introduced might not show any good effects, I would inevitably find myself in an awkward situation.

"We have already sent many people out to search," the Empress Dowager lamented to me, "hoping to find a hair dye that neither damages the hair nor stains the scalp, but we have yet to find one, and perhaps never will!"

"This servant can find such a hair dye for the Empress Dowager!" I couldn't help but volunteer.

Her old self smiled slightly upon hearing this.

"You must have seen it in those Western countries. The Westerners are indeed the most ingenious; the things they invent are often as magical as spells. I seem to have heard people say that they have many hair dyes that can be dyed into various colors according to one's wishes. I wonder which kind you are referring to?" (399)

Small Recipes

New Autumn Delicacies 153

— Yi Qiu

The sweltering heat has passed, and the auspicious New Autumn has arrived. I would like to introduce several kinds of Ping-style delicacies to celebrate the coming of autumn. According to legend, the recipes were passed down from the nobility of Beiping. Even the pastry shops in Beiping do not sell them, making them especially precious. Due to space constraints, I will select one of the easier to make and more delicious recipes to introduce below.

Gusao Cakes Prepare the ingredients: two catties of flour, twelve taels of white sugar, half a catty of walnut kernels, four taels of white sesame seeds, one and a half catties of lard, half a spoonful of salt. Prepare the utensils: one Western-style stove or charcoal stove, one rolling pin, one large cup, one flat-bottomed iron pot (size not specified), one wooden mold (carved from fir wood into a hexagonal recessed shape, the size of a silver dollar, with the character "Fu" (福) or "Shou" (壽) engraved in the center; can be custom-made from small workshops). After preparing the ingredients and utensils, first dry-fry the flour in an ordinary iron pot until it turns yellow but not burnt. Transfer it to a large bowl to cool. Separately, remove the skin from the walnut kernels and chop them into fine pieces with a knife. Stir-fry the white sesame seeds and salt separately until cooked and finely ground (grind them with a rolling pin). Mix them together with the white sugar into the fried flour, then slowly add the rendered lard and mix well. Knead into round shapes for the filling (the size should be the same as the recessed shape in the wooden mold). Wrap the filling with dough (the thickness should be the same as wonton wrappers; the dough should be made from half raw flour, half lard, and half boiling water). Place it in the wooden mold, slightly tamp it down, then tap it out. Place it in the flat-bottomed iron pot and bake until both sides are golden brown. It is now complete. The taste is delicious and palatable, with absolutely no overly sweet or greasy taste. A seasonal product for autumn.

Jujube Cakes Prepare the ingredients: one and a half catties of red dates, two catties of rice flour, one catty of brown sugar, half a catty of walnut kernels, half a catty of lard. Prepare the utensils: wooden mold, steamer, rolling pin. Once the ingredients and utensils are ready, you can begin working. Mix two catties of rice flour with about one rice bowl of water. Cook the red dates until tender, remove the skin and pits, and mix them together with the brown sugar. Knead into round shapes and then roll them out with a rolling pin to make the outer skin of the jujube cakes. Separately, cut the raw lard into small squares and chop the walnut kernels into small pieces, then mix them together to make the filling. Pass them through the wooden mold and then steam them in a steamer for half an hour. They can then be taken out and eaten. The taste is especially exquisite and cannot be compared to any sweets sold in the market. The above amounts of ingredients are for making eighty cakes. If you want to make more or less, you can increase or decrease the ingredients accordingly.

Lotus Root Cakes Use the middle section of fresh pond lotus root, peel and wash it thoroughly. Rub it frequently in a rice washing basket to make lotus root paste. Mix it with an equal amount of rice flour, add white sugar, and then fry it in a pot with lard. The flavor is particularly unique, with a glutinous, smooth, and refreshing taste upon entering the mouth. I am fond of eating it, and every autumn, I make sure my family prepares it because it tastes delicious and the method is easy.

Shen Bao Medical Weekly

Discussion on Typhoid Fever 5 (Part 1) (Taiyang Stage) 154

— Yu Yunxiu

The most incomprehensible part of the Treatise on Typhoid Fever is "chest bind (結胸)." Regarding the causes of chest bind, it states: "When the disease manifests in the yang and is treated with purgatives, heat enters and forms a chest bind... the reason for forming a chest bind is due to premature purgation." It also states: "In Taiyang disease, the pulse is floating and rapid... if the doctor uses purgatives, the rapid pulse becomes slow, there is pain resisting pressure inside the diaphragm, the stomach is empty and deficient, pathogenic qi moves the diaphragm, causing shortness of breath, restlessness, agitation, vexation in the chest, and the yang qi sinks inward, leading to hardness below the heart, which results in chest bind." Furthermore, it states: "If in typhoid fever on the fifth or sixth day, there is vomiting and fever, use Chaihu Decoction. If the symptoms are present but purgatives are used... if there is fullness and hard pain below the heart, this is chest bind." It also states: "When Taiyang and Shaoyang diseases coexist and purgatives are used, chest bind forms." This refers to chest bind resulting from misapplication of purgatives. However, it also states: "In typhoid fever on the sixth or seventh day, there is heat and substantiality in the chest bind." This indicates that chest bind can occur without the misapplication of purgatives. Cheng Wuji notes: "This does not mention purgation, but says typhoid fever on the sixth or seventh day, which is the actual heat of transmission." Zhang Jianshan notes: "Early purgation leading to chest bind is the norm, while substantial chest bind is a change in circumstances." Cheng Jiaoqian's Treatise on Typhoid Fever Postscript states: "Chest bind... need not be caused by misapplication of purgatives; typhoid fever can directly lead to chest bind on the sixth or seventh day." Wang Lingyou's Differentiation and Pattern Seat notes: "These words on chest bind indicate that there are cases that do not arise from misapplication of purgatives." All of these interpret Zhongjing's statement as referring to chest bind that arises without the misapplication of purgatives. The Treatise on Typhoid Fever also states: "For cold substantial chest bind without heat signs, Three-Ingredient Minor Qi-Invigorating Decoction (三物小陷胸湯) or White Powder (白散) may also be administered." The Song Dynasty edition of the Treatise on Typhoid Fever has a note below this passage: "One source says Three-Ingredient Minor White Powder (三物小白散)." According to the notes, this is correct, but the character "minor (小)" is redundant. Examining the Jade Box Classic (玉函經) and the Supplementary Prescriptions of a Thousand Gold Pieces (千金翼), there is no Qi-Invigorating Decoction or the phrase "may also be administered." Instead, it is written as "Three-Ingredient Minor White Powder," which agrees with what the notes refer to as "one source." The Medical Mirror (醫宗金鑑) also states: "Three-Ingredient Minor Qi-Invigorating Decoction should be Three-Ingredient White Powder." You Zaijing's Collection of Penetrating Pearls (尤在涇貫珠集) also states: "The characters 'Minor Qi-Invigorating Decoction and may also be administered' are likely redundant." Pang Anshi's General Treatise on Diseases (總病論) is written as "Three-Ingredient White Powder," with a note below stating: "Minor Qi-Invigorating Decoction is incorrect." Xu Lingtai's Classified Prescriptions (類方) has a note below White Powder stating: "According to the Living People's Book (活人書), Three-Ingredient White Powder is administered; there is no Minor Qi-Invigorating Decoction. The phrase 'may also be used' indicates that the minor qi-invigorating decoction is a cold remedy and not suitable for cases without heat." The Jade Box Classic is a different version of the Treatise on Typhoid Fever. The content recorded in the Supplementary Prescriptions of a Thousand Gold Pieces is the Treatise on Typhoid Fever of the Tang Dynasty. Zhu Fengyi's Living People's Book and Pang Anshi's General Treatise on Diseases are both from the Song Dynasty, and their content can be relied upon. Therefore, they should be followed. Furthermore, there is no Major White Powder (大白散) in the Treatise on Typhoid Fever, so the character "minor (小)" in the Jade Box Classic and the Supplementary Prescriptions of a Thousand Gold Pieces is also redundant. The Living People's Book and the General Treatise on Diseases should be followed. This chest bind is also not caused by early purgation, and seems to be related to being irrigated with cold water. To summarize the above, the Treatise on Typhoid Fever states that the origin of chest bind is often due to early purgation in typhoid fever, but there are also other causes. Chest bind that arises from heat is "heat substantial chest bind," while chest bind that arises from cold is "cold substantial chest bind."

Regarding the symptoms of chest bind, it states: "Pressing on it causes pain, the cun pulse is floating, and the guan pulse is deep. This is called chest bind." It also states: "In chest bind, the neck is also stiff, resembling a soft spasm." Furthermore, it states: "In chest bind, the pulse is floating and large. Purgation is contraindicated, as it will lead to death." Also, "When all the symptoms of chest bind are present, agitation also leads to death." Moreover, "In Taiyang disease, the pulse is floating and rapid... if the doctor uses purgatives, the rapid pulse becomes slow, there is pain resisting pressure inside the diaphragm, the stomach is empty and deficient, pathogenic qi moves the diaphragm, causing shortness of breath, restlessness, agitation, vexation in the chest, and the yang qi sinks inward, leading to hardness below the heart, which results in chest bind." Also, "In heat substantial chest bind, the pulse is deep and tight, there is pain below the heart, and it is as hard as stone when pressed." Furthermore, "If there is no bowel movement for five or six days, the tongue is dry and parched, there is slight tidal fever in the afternoon, and hardness and fullness extend from below the heart to the lower abdomen, with pain that is unbearable to touch." It also states: "In minor chest bind, the disease is located below the heart, pressing on it causes pain, and the pulse is floating and slippery." To summarize the above symptoms, the pulse cannot be relied upon, as the cun and guan positions do not have two separate levels. Floating means floating in both positions, and deep means deep in both positions. There is no such thing as a cun pulse that is floating and a guan pulse that is deep. "Hardness and fullness extending from below the heart to the lower abdomen, with pain that is unbearable to touch" and "pain below the heart that is as hard as stone when pressed" are the primary symptoms. Any case of typhoid fever that develops these symptoms due to purgation is a case of peritonitis due to intestinal perforation, and is extremely dangerous. Therefore, the Bright Theory (明理論) states: "In typhoid fever, chest bind is the most dreaded condition." The Essential Points of Typhoid Fever (傷寒廣要) states: "In typhoid fever, chest bind is a dreaded symptom." As for neck stiffness and agitation, these indicate that the disease has invaded the brain. Therefore, the Treatise on Typhoid Fever states: "Agitation leads to death." You Zaijing's Collection of Penetrating Pearls states: "Severe neck stiffness indicates severe chest bind." This is peritonitis due to intestinal perforation that has progressed to meningitis. Intestinal perforation in typhoid fever need not be caused by misapplication of purgatives, and can also occur spontaneously. The "substantial chest bind" mentioned in the Treatise on Typhoid Fever refers to this condition. Cold substantial chest bind and minor chest bind are obstructions in the stomach and are not peritonitis due to intestinal perforation. Furthermore, a rapid pulse turning slow, pain resisting pressure inside the diaphragm, shortness of breath, restlessness, agitation, and vexation in the chest are precursors to jaundice, and the symptoms are often like this, resembling chest bind. Therefore, it says: "Yang qi sinks inward, leading to hardness below the heart, which results in chest bind," indicating that the presence of these prodromal symptoms, followed by hardness below the heart, constitutes chest bind. In reality, typhoid fever patients who develop jaundice often have these symptoms. Zhongjing saw that it did not develop into chest bind but rather into jaundice. Therefore, it says: "If there is no chest bind... the body will develop jaundice." This passage is actually describing the symptoms of jaundice, which Zhongjing mistakenly thought was going to develop into chest bind. Chest bind is peritonitis due to intestinal perforation, and the pulse is inevitably thin and rapid. Therefore, the Essential Meanings of Typhoid Fever (傷寒蘊要) states: "A faint, thready, deep pulse and cold hands and feet indicate a difficult prognosis." The Clear Essentials of Typhoid Fever (傷寒證治明條) states: "A deep, faint, thready, and small pulse indicates certain death." However, a rapid pulse turning slow is a characteristic symptom of jaundice, as the pulse in jaundice is often slow. If the pulse in peritonitis due to intestinal perforation turns slow, it inevitably progresses to meningitis, or it may be so. There is no case where the pulse turns slow before the onset of peritonitis due to intestinal perforation.

By examining both the causes and symptoms, it is clear that chest bind is peritonitis due to intestinal perforation. The only hope for survival in peritonitis due to intestinal perforation is surgical intervention to cleanse the contamination, and it certainly cannot be cured with Qi-Invigorating Pills or Qi-Invigorating Decoctions. The statement that "Qi-Invigorating Pills and Qi-Invigorating Decoctions should be used" is not a treatment method. Furthermore, since this disease is caused by purgation, how can it be cured by further purgation? This is what I mean by incomprehensible.

Harvey, the Discoverer of Blood Circulation 155

— Yue Qi

——Medical Stories 8——

Scientists, calling themselves natural philosophers in ancient Greece and Rome, were deeply interested in the various constant and involuntary movements of the living body. Some of these movements they saw in other people's bodies, and some they perceived in their own bodies. For example: the bellows-like movement of the chest during breathing; the heartbeat and pulse, which they regarded as unrelated to each other; when the skin broke, blood would seep out or gush out, as if the skin itself were full of blood. In the abdomen, they also felt the movements of various internal organs, such as the spasms and peristalsis of the intestines, and the movement of food, etc.

These objective and clear facts naturally needed to be explained. For the natural philosophers of the time, the only possible method was to dissect animal corpses. Due to religious and social concerns and restrictions, they could not examine human corpses. They also could not keep animals alive while dissecting their bodies in order to observe the true activity of the organs. So-called experimental physiology was unknown at the time. Therefore, the ways in which they inferred the activity of living organs from the dissection of lifeless organs were mostly wrong.

Of all these movements, what interested them the most was the movement of the heart and lungs, and the relationship of these movements to blood. From animal dissections, they could easily see that there was a diaphragm separating the chest and abdomen; the air entering and leaving the body passed through the lungs; and the heart was closely attached to the lungs. They did not understand the chemical transformation of inhaled and exhaled air, and assumed the function of the lungs was like a fan, cooling the overheated blood. Black blood was always seen in the veins and the right ventricle of the heart; sometimes a little blood was seen in the left ventricle of the heart; but in the arteries, they saw only air. Therefore, they imagined that the veins transported blood from the lungs to various tissues, and the arteries transported air from the lungs to various tissues.

Galen assumed that the heart was the source of body heat, and blood was the fuel to aid heat. He posed a question to himself: why did the blood in the right and left ventricles of the heart have different colors and densities? His answer came entirely from imagination. He assumed that the blood was filtered as it passed through the small pores in the septum between the right and left ventricles. He certainly could not see these pores, but he said that although you cannot see the pores of the skin, you know that sweat seeps out from the pores of the skin.

These erroneous ideas about blood circulation prevailed for hundreds of years. The credit for establishing the true theory of blood circulation goes to William Harvey. His discovery is one of the important foundations of modern medicine and modern biology. After putting forward the idea that blood circulates throughout the body, people were able to imagine that blood transports nutrients from the digestive tissues and gas from the lungs to various tissues, and also transports waste and toxins to the kidneys, ready to be excreted from the body.

The establishment of the theory that the heart propels blood was very slow. The authoritative medical circles of the Middle Ages blindly followed Galen's theory. Harvey was the first to realize that blood is propelled by the heart to form a systemic circulation. He once said: "I observed the beating heart of animals, and at first imagined that the movement of the heart could only be understood by God, because the contraction and expansion of the heart were so rapid that I could not see when this contraction and expansion occurred." However, he finally pointed out: (1) at the same instant the heart contracts, the artery also beats once; (2) when the artery ruptures, blood spurts out once for each heart contraction; (3) when the heart stops beating at the moment of death, the pulse also stops at the same time. His conclusion was this: the blood vessels are divided into two groups, the arteries carry blood away from the heart, and the veins carry blood into the heart: the black venous blood enters the right side of the heart, passes through the lungs, and turns into bright red blood due to the action of fresh air, returns to the left side of the heart, and is transported to various parts of the body by the arteries. As for how blood flows from the arteries to the veins, this question was not resolved until nine years later when Malpighi discovered capillaries—the slender vessels that connect the small arteries and small veins.

The first powerful evidence proving the circulation theory was the total amount of blood in the body. According to experiments, the heart pumps out one-quarter of an ounce of blood with each beat. According to this calculation, in half an hour, the heart contracts a thousand times, and must pump out ten pounds and five ounces of blood. However, the total amount of blood in the body averages only seven and a half ounces: if the blood were not circulating, there would be no way to resolve the question of how the amount of blood pumped out by the heart exceeds the total amount of blood in the body.

Common Knowledge Q&A on Diseases 156

— Cheng Hanzhang

(65) Acute Localized Peritonitis

(Acute Circumscribed Peritonitis)

Q: What is acute localized peritonitis?

A: This is a type of suppurative peritonitis, where the affected area is confined to a local part of the peritoneum, forming a tumor or abscess.

Q: What is the difference between the abdominal symptoms and those of acute generalized peritonitis?

A: The abdominal symptoms are the same as those of generalized peritonitis, but the pain and tenderness are confined to one area, where a tumor with dullness on percussion and fluctuation is formed.

Q: What is the difference between the systemic symptoms of the patient and those of acute generalized peritonitis?

A: The systemic symptoms are also very similar to those of acute generalized peritonitis, but the degree is lighter, and most of the fevers are irregular, resembling remittent fever.

Q: What is the course of suppurative localized peritonitis?

Page 16

A: During the course of the disease, if it can be absorbed, it will be cured; if the disease is prolonged for too long, it will cause general weakness, collapse, and death. Or, it may form an abscess. Some result in scar healing and induration; some cause perforation of the peritoneum, resulting in sepsis.

Q: What are the more important locations where peritoneal abscesses occur?

A: Abscesses under the diaphragm are more important, because if they expand to the right, they can cause secondary abscesses of the right lobe of the liver, the biliary tract, the appendix, or the right kidney; if they invade to the left, they can cause secondary abscesses of the stomach and duodenum, the left lobe of the liver, the spleen, the pancreas, the left kidney, or the pericardium.

Q: What are the symptoms of acute localized peritonitis?

A: The onset is acute or insidious, starting with chills and shivering, with localized abdominal pain and tenderness. The skin in the area of pain, in the region of the costal arch, is swollen, and sometimes the lower part of the rib cage or the intercostal spaces expand. The movement of the diaphragm is reduced; therefore, the lower border of the lung does not move during breathing.

Q: When diagnosing acute localized peritonitis, what diseases should it be differentiated from?

A: A rectal or vaginal examination should be performed to differentiate it from a pregnant uterus, a bladder full of urine, or tympanites. It should also be differentiated from empyema, pyopneumothorax, liver abscess, hydatid cyst, perirenal abscess, etc.

Q: What is the best treatment for acute localized peritonitis?

A: It is best to perform surgical drainage early.

Q: How should the patient be cared for?

A: The patient should be kept absolutely quiet and lying flat. An ice pack or warm compress should be applied to the abdomen.

Q: What medications should be taken internally?

A: Mainly pain relievers. For vomiting, use chloroform water or cocaine gastric lavage. For hiccups, use atropine injections. For paralytic ileus, use Physostigmine, Eumydrin, Atropine, etc. to wash the intestines.

Q: What medications should be used for heart failure or collapse?

A: Injections of camphor preparations, caffeine, cardiazole, etc. Or, use physiological saline, Ringer's solution, Locke's solution, etc., plus epinephrine diluted to one thousandth (1 ml) for intravenous injection. (End)

Postscript to the Compilation of Medical Lawsuits 157

— Song Guobin

After I finished editing the Compilation of Medical Lawsuits, I lingered in my room, pondering and searching, and finally stood up and said: "There are so many cases of medical malpractice lawsuits, and the background is so complex. To remove the fruit, one must first eliminate the cause; to stop the flow, one must first cool the source. If we want to quell the litigious wind and pacify the medical profession, how can our colleagues not fully understand the causes and effects of the numerous medical disputes and think about ways to prevent them?" Please, based on this principle, let me briefly state them:

What is the cause? It is the background. The background of medical lawsuits is not just one aspect. Roughly divided, there are four: Since the establishment of the lawyer system, the people have begun to enjoy legal rights. Corrupt officials who used to manipulate the law can no longer act arbitrarily without any scruples! However, law is a tool to govern people, and its use depends on the individual. Lawyers use the law as their profession. The wise can be fair and honest, aiming to protect human rights. However, due to business reasons, some may resort to inciting discord to achieve their own private interests. As a result, there are more and more lawsuits in society, and doctors are the first to bear the brunt! This is the first. Zhang Shizhi said, "The Minister of Justice holds the balance of the world." Today's courts are what was called the Minister of Justice in ancient times. If the people have grievances, they will appeal to the law. If the judgment is improper, they will immediately seek redress. To prevent grievances, it depends on the judge's careful handling of the case. However, today's judges, in medical cases, lightly accept the case without asking whether the defendant is a licensed physician. Once accepted, they listen only to the emotional pleas of the patient's family and ignore the medical basis. The judgment is difficult to convince people, and appeals are endless. This is the second. Journalists wield the authority of public opinion, which is enough to shift social perceptions. However, when medical cases occur, they always adopt an attitude of recording everything they hear, and they make untrue reports without waiting for the truth to be clarified. This reduces the reputation of the medical profession and the sympathy of society. This is the third. Furthermore, I have heard, "Wood must rot before insects appear, and a country must attack itself before others attack it." The lack of unity within the medical profession is also a cause of lawsuits. When united, strength gathers; when divided, power scatters. Therefore, medical factions exist, and the unity of the medical profession is weakened day by day. Disputes over rights arise, and some even use others to suppress colleagues from different factions due to temporary emotions. If the internal situation is like this, what else can be said? This is the fourth. Summarizing these four points, we can call them the background. As for the way to prevent lawsuits and eliminate unjust cases, there are several ways. Please allow me to elaborate further:

Medicine is a highly specialized science. Whether a patient's failure to recover or death is due to the doctor or the disease cannot be determined by non-experts. Although judges are familiar with the articles of the law, they are not familiar with medical principles. Therefore, when accepting a case, they must consult a formal medical organization to make a fair assessment as a basis for judgment. At the same time, an autopsy must be performed to reveal the truth. Judges must not have any arbitrary attitude in this process. However, what if the judge still acts according to their own will despite the assessment and autopsy? This is why the jury system and compensation for unjust cases must be implemented. With the participation of expert medical examiners, judges will not overstep their authority, and the questioning will be relevant. With compensation for unjust cases, the patient's family will not dare to make false accusations lightly, and judges will not dare to arbitrarily sentence people. Assessment, autopsy, jury, and compensation, the gradual implementation of these four aspects may eliminate medical disputes to some extent. As for the group, it must be united and not easily allow others to take advantage. As for the individual, they must be vigilant and not be negligent in the slightest. This is something that colleagues who read this book should know on their own, and I need not repeat it. Postscript by Song Guobin, September 1, Year 24.

Popular Lecture on Modern Venereology (15) 158

— Compiled by Chen Shengbai, Corrected by Yin Muqiang

Part Three: Chancroid

The sites of occurrence of chancroid are mainly in the genital area, such as the coronal sulcus, inner surface or tip of the foreskin in men, glans penis, frenulum, external urethral orifice, penile skin and scrotum. In women, it occurs in the posterior commissure (the area between the vulva and anus), external urethral orifice, vaginal opening, external cervical os, and labia.

The symptoms of chancroid vary slightly depending on the site of occurrence. I will list them as follows:

A. In men, when it occurs on the frenulum, the frenulum may be completely eroded or only the bridge-shaped frenulum may remain. This type of chancroid is prone to complications of buboes.

B. When it occurs on the inner surface of the foreskin, the swelling is obvious, and pus easily accumulates, resembling phimosis. At this time, the glans penis may be damaged, leading to necrosis of the entire foreskin and glans penis.

C. When it starts on the glans penis, the symptoms are relatively mild. However, in some cases, it can invade the corpus cavernosum of the penis, leading to gangrene and shedding.

D. When it occurs on the neck of the glans penis, it often spreads around the glans penis in a ring shape, causing ulceration of the external urethral orifice.

E. In women, it often spreads around the labia and vulva.

F. When it occurs on the greater vestibular gland in the vulva, it initially appears as a hard nodule, which later becomes an ulcer, characterized by a volcano-like appearance.

G. When it occurs on the labia minora and clitoris, the swelling is obvious, similar to that occurring on the inner surface of the foreskin in men.

H. When it occurs in the vagina, it is not easily invaded due to its multi-layered squamous epithelial tissue. If it does occur, it must be in the lower or inner part.

The course of chancroid usually takes two to three weeks to seven to eight weeks for complete recovery. However, when new chancroids continue to appear, the course is very long.

C. Diagnosis and Prognosis: The diagnosis of chancroid can be made based on the short incubation period and the unique ulcer state. As for the differential diagnosis, it has been described in detail in the first part with the hard chancre of syphilis. It can be distinguished from the papules of syphilis in the genital area by the non-ulceration of syphilitic papules and the positive Wassermann serological reaction. As for distinguishing it from other diseases, those who understand the unique symptoms and unique reactions of each disease can easily handle it like a butcher dissecting an ox with ease.

The prognosis of chancroid is generally good. However, in cases of serpiginous spread, erosive or gangrenous changes, there may be residual organic defects after healing, or septicemia or massive hemorrhage leading to death.

Common Knowledge of Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Hygiene 159

— Tang Renjin

(61) Dacryocystitis

Dacryocystitis, also known as acute dacryocystitis, or dacryocystic cellulitis, is mostly caused by the transformation of chronic dacryocystitis. Because when suffering from chronic dacryocystitis, its mucous membrane is easily damaged, so that bacteria easily get the opportunity to invade the tissues and develop abscesses. In addition, syphilitic periostitis and glandular periostitis can also induce cellulitis in the lacrimal sac area. The symptoms of this disease are very obvious. At the beginning of its onset, there is severe pain in the lacrimal sac area, and the skin becomes red and swollen. In severe cases, conjunctival, eyelid, or facial edema can also occur. The patient has a fever and restless sleep. After two or three days, the skin of the lacrimal sac area turns yellow, and then it ruptures spontaneously, draining a large amount of pus. At this time, the pain suddenly stops, and the swelling also gradually disappears. The ruptured wound can often turn into a fistula, constantly flowing out pus-like liquid, and then turning into serous-like, and finally turning into watery liquid. This is called a lacrimal fistula. The fistula does not necessarily occur in the lacrimal sac area, but also in its vicinity. Sometimes, although the fistula has closed, the nasolacrimal duct is still not unobstructed, so that it is inevitable to occur again very much. Sometimes the fistula exists for life, and serous or watery liquid often flows out of the ruptured hole.

The treatment principle of lacrimal sac abscess. First, of course, quickly treat chronic dacryocystitis to prevent inducing this disease. Second, before the skin has been destroyed, we should try to drain the liquid accumulated in the lacrimal sac. Third, if the pain is severe and the skin has already turned yellow, it is a clear proof that it has already suppurated. At this time, an incision can be made in the anterior wall of the lacrimal sac to drain the pus. Fourth, if the lacrimal fistula has been around for a long time or is difficult to cure, the lacrimal sac must be removed by resection. This is the best policy.

Medical Treatment for Pain (29) 160

— Li Xing

Childbirth Pain

It is inevitable that women will suffer some pain during childbirth. Childbirth pain is a physiological function. Normal labor lasts about half a day to one and a half days. The first childbirth is more painful. As for why childbirth is painful, most people do not fully understand. The origin of the pain is the intermittent contraction of the uterus. The baby's head is larger than the diameter of the birth canal before delivery, so there must be intermittent contractions to squeeze the baby's head smaller to fit the size of the birth canal. The several long bones of the baby's head were originally movable. The intermittent contractions of the uterus gradually force them tighter, and the large bones of the head overlap at the long bone joints, so the diameter of the head is reduced. The birth canal is not a straight road. With the contraction of the uterus, the head and neck also bend and move down the birth canal. The head must reach a certain position, otherwise it will be a difficult labor.

This is entirely a physiological function. The contraction of the uterus (i.e., pain) shrinks the baby's head. Then, through the birth canal, the head reaches a certain position. The cervix also gradually expands. Until all the functions reach a certain limit, the baby's head is forced out of the birth canal. Then the baby's body follows, and the baby is completely born. After the baby is born, after a few minutes to more than twenty minutes, a relatively peaceful pain arises again until the placenta is expelled, and the childbirth pain comes to an end.

Difficult labor is not only painful, but also sometimes life-threatening. In less severe difficult labor, the mother suffers some pain, and then she can safely pass through. As for absolute difficult labor, without special surgery, both mother and child will be injured.

Primitive men and women lived a rough life, and their whole body muscles were fully developed, healthy, and strong. In the event of childbirth, the muscles contract powerfully and freely. Childbirth can be completed in a short period of time without special pain. The red Indians in South America today still live in ancient times, and these women have childbirth very easily. Even the women in our country who work in the countryside do not consider childbirth as anything special. Those who have more difficult and painful childbirths are those who live comfortable lives now. Their muscles are very underdeveloped and inactive, so childbirth is not very easy.

Economic Special Issue

The Issue of Maturity Period in the Pawnbroking Industry 161

— Mi Junfu

According to a survey released by the Ministry of Interior in the Republic of China in 1931, the maturity periods of the pawnbroking industry in 15 cities including Shanghai are as follows:

Three-month maturity: Qingdao, 33 establishments. Six-month maturity: Guangzhou, 54 establishments. Eight-month maturity: Guangzhou, 3 establishments. (Editor's note: The original table totaled 62 establishments, it is unknown which is correct.) One-year maturity: Guangzhou, 139 establishments, Xiamen, 5 establishments, Shenyang, 50 establishments, Yingkou, 9 establishments, Andong, 12 establishments, Chengdu, 25 establishments. Total: 240 establishments. Thirteen-month maturity: Qingdao, 2 establishments. Eighteen-month maturity: Shanghai, 48 establishments, Nanjing, 8 establishments, Tianjin, 13 establishments, Hangzhou, 19 establishments, Ningbo, 10 establishments, Shenyang, 5 establishments, Andong, 2 establishments, Chengdu, 12 establishments, Chongqing, 9 establishments. Total: 126 establishments. (The original text says 130 establishments, it is unknown which is wrong, editor's note again.) Two-year maturity: Beiping, 105 establishments, Tianjin, 12 establishments, Guangzhou, 5 establishments, Xiamen, 6 establishments, Jinan, 5 establishments. Total: 133 establishments.

Statistical Table of Maturity Periods of Pawnbroking Industry in 16 Provinces including Jiangsu

According to the above table, except for the pawnbroking maturity period of three months in Qingdao and 40 days in Liaoning, which were established by the Japanese. The shortest pawnbroking maturity period in our country is six months, and the longest is three years. The most common are twelve months, thirteen months, eighteen months, and twenty-four months. Of the 654 pawnbroking establishments surveyed in 15 cities including Shanghai, the percentages of maturity periods are shown in the following table:

Maturity Period Establishments Percentage of Total Establishments Surveyed Maturity Period Establishments Percentage of Total Establishments Surveyed

12 Months 240 36.7% (weak) 24 Months 123 20% (strong)

18 Months 130 20% (weak) Total 503 76.7% (strong)

The percentages of maturity periods of the 1,281 pawnbroking establishments surveyed in 16 provinces including Jiangsu Province are shown in the following table.

Maturity Period Establishments Percentage of Total Establishments Surveyed Maturity Period Establishments Percentage of Total Establishments Surveyed

12 Months 355 27.7% (strong) 24 Months 102 8% (weak)

13 Months 269 21% Total 963 75.2% (strong)

18 Months 237 18.5% (strong)

Of these, it is worth noting that the number of establishments with a maturity period of 12 months accounts for the largest number in this survey. A total of 595 establishments in provinces and cities. If 13 months is added, there are a total of 864 establishments, accounting for 44.7% (weak) of the total number of pawnbroking establishments surveyed in provinces and cities (1,935 establishments), approximately half. The number of establishments with a maturity period of 18 months is 367 in total in provinces and cities, accounting for 18.9% (strong) of the total number of pawnbroking establishments surveyed in provinces and cities. The number of establishments with a maturity period of 24 months is 235 in total in provinces and cities, accounting for 12% (strong) of the total number of pawnbroking establishments surveyed in provinces and cities.

Another point to note is that the maturity period of urban pawnshops is often shorter than that of rural pawnshops. Farmers pledge money in the spring and only have money to redeem it in the autumn harvest. If the harvest this autumn is not good, they will postpone the redemption until the next autumn. Their ability to redeem is limited by the season. The pawnbroking customers in urban areas are mostly small industrial and commercial operators or poor citizens, whose income has no seasonal relationship and can redeem it as soon as they pawn it. In this respect, urban pawnshops and rural pawnshops are fundamentally different in nature. The maturity period of both must be stipulated separately according to their nature. According to the above-mentioned survey: Of the maturity periods of pawnshops in 15 cities including Shanghai, 36.7% of the surveyed establishments have a maturity period of 12 months. Of the rural pawnshops, 27.7% have a maturity period of 12 months. The former percentage is obviously higher than the latter. The longest maturity period for urban pawnshops is 24 months, while the longest maturity period for rural pawnshops is 36 months.

The provisions on the maturity period in the separate regulations of the pawnbroking industry in various provinces differ slightly from the above-mentioned actual situation. The following is an excerpt from the provisions on the maturity period in the separate regulations of the pawnbroking industry in various provinces surveyed by the author in 1934:

Location Pawn (or Pledge)

Jiangsu Eleven months (retained for another six months)

Shanghai Eighteen months Eight months

Zhejiang Eighteen months

Anhui Eighteen months

Wuyang, Hubei Six months

Hunan Ten months Seven months

Fujian Twenty months

Guangdong (Pawn) Three years (Pledge) Two years One year or less Six months

Yunnan Six months

Kunming Twelve months

Shandong Thirteen months

Qingdao Thirteen months

Shaanxi Twenty months

Jehol Twelve months Ten months

Guizhou (Pawn) Twenty-seven months (Pledge) Thirteen months (Pledge) Twelve months (Pledge) Ten months

Shanxi Six months

Guangxi Twelve months

Hebei Eighteen months

According to the above table, the regulations on the maturity period in the separate regulations of the pawnbroking industry in various provinces and cities differ slightly from the actual situation. However, except for small pledges, they are generally more than twelve months, with some as long as three years. Whether this maturity period is appropriate depends on the interests of both the pawnbroking industry and the pawn customer, and the type of pawned goods. The following lists the maturity periods of pawnshops in various important countries for reference:

Table of Maturity Periods of Profit-Making Pawnshops in Major Countries Country Maturity Period

United Kingdom One year and seven days

United States Twelve to eighteen months (different in each state, this is based on the draft standard pawnshop rules)

Germany Six months to one year

Japan Ordinary four months to six months Table of Maturity Periods of Public Welfare Pawnshops in Major Countries

France Ordinary one year

Switzerland Six months

Belgium One year

Germany Ordinary six months to one year

Austria One year

Japan Four months

Illinois, USA One year

According to the above two tables, it can be seen that the ordinary maturity period for pawnshops in various countries, whether private or public, is one year, which is roughly similar to the situation in our country.

The general situation of the maturity period is as described above. The following discusses what is the appropriate number of months for the maturity period in our country. The following is an exploration from various aspects:

First, thinking from the perspective of the pawn customer

The reason why the shortest maturity period is stipulated in the pawnbroking regulations is originally for the protection of the pawn customer, which is the same as the intention of stipulating the highest interest rate. Although the pawn customer and the pawnbroker are nominally in an equal position and trade freely. However, in fact, the pawn customer is often in a disadvantageous position compared to the pawnbroker due to the urgency of needing money and the weakness of economic strength. Therefore, national legislation is necessary to protect the weak. If the maturity period is too short, the opportunity to redeem is reduced, and the loss to the pawn customer is great. Take Japan as an example: In Japan, in 1906, the ordinary maturity period in Tokyo was eight months. The ratio of the value of pawned goods to the total amount of loans was 7%. Later, the maturity period was gradually shortened. This ratio also gradually increased. By 1913, the ordinary maturity period was four to six months, and the ratio of the value of pawned goods to the total amount of loans increased to 12%. Therefore, Article 8 of the Japanese Public Welfare Pawnbroking Law stipulates:

"The maturity period shall not be less than four months from the date of establishment of the pledge contract. If the maturity period is less than four months, it shall be changed to four months."

The above-mentioned article is compulsory in nature. It is a typical regulation to stipulate the maturity period to protect the interests of the pawn customer. However, if the maturity period is too long, the interest increases with time, making the pawn customer unable to redeem, which is also detrimental to the pawn customer.

Second, thinking from the perspective of the pawnbroking industry

From the perspective of the pawnbroking industry, shortening the maturity period is more beneficial. (A) The storage time of the pawned goods is short, the style has not yet become outdated, and it is easier to sell. (B) Recover the loan in a short period of time and provide it for use again, and the capital turnover is active. (C) If the pawned goods are commodities or agricultural products, the price changes are small, and there is no unexpected loss. However, what is the purpose of the pawnbroking business? It is to collect interest, not to profit from the disposal of pawned goods. Moreover, at this time when the disposal of pawned goods is extremely difficult, the pawnbroker is making every effort to reduce the number of pawned goods. If the maturity period is too short, there will be more pawned goods. Therefore, it is not only unfavorable to the pawn customer, but also not what the pawnbroker wants.

Third, observing from the historical evolution

Commercial behavior is gradually becoming more complex and seeking agility due to social and economic relations. Financial institutions are the center of commerce. Therefore, commercial banks mainly provide short-term loans. Although our country's pawnshops mainly provide consumer funds and rural loans, there is also a trend of gradually shortening the loan period. For example, in Hubei, the pawnbroking period was 16 months in the Qing Dynasty. In 1927, it was changed to 12 months. Now in Wuyang, it has been shortened to 6 months. In Japan, the pawnbroking period was 12 months in the Tokugawa era. In the early Meiji era, it was 8 months. Now it has been shortened to four to six months. The trace of evolution is clearly visible. In our country's pawnbroking, the general public psychology is that most people have a maturity period of 18 months, but according to the above-mentioned survey, it is known that a maturity period of 12 months is already more common than 18 months.

Summarizing the above points, a maturity period that is too long is not only detrimental to both the pawn customer and the pawnbroking industry, but also inconsistent with modern social and economic relations. Therefore, theoretically speaking, it is necessary to shorten the maturity period of more than 18 months. Furthermore, based on the facts, most countries have a maturity period of 12 months. In our country, the current customs in various places and the separate regulations of various provinces and cities also have the most maturity periods of 12 months. Therefore, in the future, the maturity period of pawnbroking in our country should be determined to be 12 months as the standard, and then it should be determined in consideration of the local situation (different urban and rural areas) and the type of pawned goods (such as agricultural products should be determined according to the season and modern women's clothing changes too quickly, the period should be shortened).

1929-32

Among the above textile fibers, rayon has made rapid progress in the past. In the past year, the total world output has reached 7.91 million bales. The success of this emerging textile fiber is due in part to the improvement in quality; in part to the large manufacturers using their incentive policies to reduce costs for customers. As a result, rayon has taken over the original markets of cotton, silk, and wool. Therefore, the increase in cotton prices has indirectly caused rayon to take its place and replace it. As far as we know, the United States government has consulted with various governments on an international plan to limit cotton production. However, no country has agreed to this unnatural restriction. They all hope to share the remaining profits after the United States reduces production. Therefore, if the United States continues to use restrictions to raise cotton prices, this is a policy that is unlikely to be successful! (The End)

Introduction to the Newly Published Supplement to Chinese Rural Economic Data 163

Mr. Feng Hefa studies rural economics and can collect and discuss the conditions of rural areas in various places. He is down-to-earth and does not favor empty talk, which is different from those who like to talk loftily at the moment. Ningbo Banks Recall Loans 165

The long-term loans issued by various banks and money shops in Shanghai on behalf of Ningbo banks are substantial, estimated to be no less than 30 million. Now that a financial crisis has occurred in Ningbo, there are plans to recall most of these loans in order to maintain stability. Therefore, letters have been sent to the Shanghai agents of various banks, urging them to find ways to recover the loans. However, Shanghai is also affected by various factors, making it difficult to achieve the desired outcome. Detailed information about these matters was recorded in this newspaper a few days ago. It is now heard from people in the industry that although these long-term loans still have more than a month before they are due, time flies quickly, and the deadline will arrive in the blink of an eye. If preparations are not made in advance, it will be difficult to resolve the situation when the time comes. Therefore, financial leaders plan to discuss and resolve the issue in the near future. The most difficult point is that this year, due to the inability of money shops to issue loans, all businesses feel financially strained, and they have no surplus to repay old debts. Moreover, these long-term loans are mostly rollovers from last year or the previous term, with new loans accounting for less than one or two tenths of the total. If strict measures are taken, there is a risk of a complete collapse. If a moderate approach is taken, Ningbo banks may not be satisfied. How can this issue be resolved? We will continue to report on this after the industry authorities have convened a meeting.

Free Talk

Leisure and Decadence 173

— Jiang Jiping

If we pay attention to the state of literature and art in each dynasty, we can deduce the rise and fall of the country. This is not superstition, but a reality, because literature and art mostly belong to the people. Whether it is prose or poetry, it mostly represents the language of the masses, so by looking at its poetry and prose, we can deduce the state of the country. The works of the early Tang poets were all majestic. Yang Jiong's poem: "Snow darkens the painted flags, the wind is mixed with the sound of drums. I would rather be a centurion than a scholar." Luo Binwang's poem: "The full moon approaches the shadow of the bow, the stars enter the sword's edge. I will not learn from Yan Dan, singing in vain the cold waters of Yi." Both have a great sense of anger and ambition. After several years, this spirit has been worn away. What remains is leisurely sentiment, decadent pleasure, and slight sorrow of parting. People seem unable to muster the energy, as if they have just recovered from illness, weak and without strength. It seems that the era forces them to act like this. We cannot blame our writers for being unenterprising in this era. It is the environment of the era that makes it so. Not only now, but every dynasty is the same. We see the works of the late Song Dynasty:

"Magnificent buildings face each other, connecting with the envoy's star, peace has been made between the north and south. We must buy wine and urge merriment. When else can we find peace?" — Song Wu Zeli's poem.

Is this situation the same as now? What people seek is just a respite of ease, confined in an ivory tower, unable to see the state of society and the country. No, perhaps they can see it, but there is always a feeling of "I can't manage so much," so they can only enjoy themselves temporarily. "A boatload of Dongting oranges has been bought, new white ramie garments are tailored in the color of snow. Calling Wu girls for a drink together, the spring breeze sends me to Jiangnan." (Wu Zeli's poem) This is truly the behavior of a young master. Some people enjoy themselves like this, while others want to leave the world, to become a hermit who escapes the world. "I have found a good place to escape Qin, peach blossoms are in spring again. Do not let the falling flowers follow the flowing water, for fear that fishermen will come to ask about the law." That era allowed escape from reality, but this era does not allow escape. If we do this, we can only wait for the demon to open its mouth and devour us. Our leisure will not last long, and this ivory tower is no place to live. We open our eyes and see:

"The thatched house and the palace turn into sunset, lonely clouds drift and what to rely on—the landscapes are originally the same, but half of the cities and people are no longer there..." — (Wen Tianxiang's poem)

How many people at this time have no home, no freedom, and nothing? We are still talking about leisure here and leisure there. This is really too much!

A Meeting with Beatrice 174

— Cao Juren

"The god of love suddenly descended at this time,

His solemn appearance when he came truly makes me afraid to recall it now."

——Dante New Life

Along the Arno River, Beatrice and I walked slowly step by step, and together got into a small boat. She was wearing a simple olive-colored gauze dress, which harmonized with the colors of the woods, hedges, and grasslands; her shadow reflected in the waves, as if the bright clouds in the sky were reflected upside down. She was silent, she stared at me with those incomparable beautiful eyes. Virgil, he had returned to the Linba residence; Beatrice accompanied me across the Arno River—the paradise on earth.

Under the intertwined locust trees, I walked with her. Cicadas were chirping on the locust trees, making this place especially quiet, and we could hear each other's breathing.

"She is a god, she is the master of nature, she is the great harmony of wisdom and beauty," I thought.

I seemed to see countless angels surrounding her, singing songs and scattering flowers. If I were dust, I would willingly let her trample on me.

"Who was that who just went back? Where did he come from with you? Where did he go back to?" she asked.

"He, Virgil, a poet and also a philosopher. He said that according to your will, he is looking after my destiny. We have traveled through the layers of hell, and we saw the words "Those who enter here, abandon all hope" on the gates of hell. Now, Virgil, he has returned to that gloomy old place."

"One, I see that you always have a melancholy face, isn't there a time when you should have a smile?"

"B, Smile? I am smiling now, in front of you. I used to believe that the dawn was not far away, and that when the sun came out, we could have a happy day. I now know that we are in the midst of a long night, and the aurora borealis occasionally shines through, but it is still so dark, without a glimmer of light."

"Are there not many companions walking in the darkness with you?"

"I remember that there was a group of people who traveled with me at the beginning. Everyone was very young, believed that they could open their eyes in the darkness, and believed that by searching and groping, they could always get out of this circle of darkness. Before long, some of my companions fled back, some fell into traps and were never seen again; and some sat there waiting for dawn. I am so lonely, without companions, groping in the dark forever."

The two of us walked to the shade of a willow tree, and I sat down with her. In front of us was a small river, the surface of the water was rippled by a gentle breeze. Above, the cicadas in this tree and the cicadas in that tree played a slow, drawn-out hissing sound. Behind us, the long-necked white geese on the leather ground came over, occasionally "flapping their wings and shouting loudly. At this time, I felt that everything before was an illusion, only this great harmony was real; but then I felt that this great harmony was an illusion, and the real thing must be those terrible nightmares. She seemed to feel the same way, she asked me:

"D, What are you thinking about?"

"What do I think about? That should be what I really think about. I used to believe that there were black and white, right and wrong, two distinct sides; I divided the people around us into two different groups, friends and enemies, and I divided what I heard and saw into two different judgments, which should be approved or opposed. I now know that it is not that simple, on the chessboard of interests, friends and enemies, approval or opposition, change in an instant, and it is simply indistinguishable. There is no reality worth my attachment, my last attachment is "love".

Beatrice listened to him with a smile, she said nothing.

"I used to be enthusiastic about politics; my father was a Guelph, so I was a Guelph too. Later, because of the fear of destruction, I felt that I should love the country, so I became a Ghibelline. When I was still a child, I saw puddles of fresh blood on the ground on the way to school every day; this terrible shadow has always disturbed me. Later, I was forced to flee the city of Florence and wandered for a long time in the ruins of Ravenna. When the youthful fervor had faded away, I withdrew from the political circles. I thought that my heart, my soul, should have a place to rest, like white clouds hiding in rocky valleys.

When I said "white clouds hiding in rocky valleys," my voice trembled a little. At this time, a strong wind was blowing, and dark clouds in the sky were flying over in clusters, and raindrops were falling from above. Raindrops were falling densely on our heads. The trees across the river were shrouded in thick fog and could not be recognized. The two of us looked at the misty rainy scene leaning on the railing. Splashing raindrops wet her hair: only a few green flies were circling around the table, and the white geese were flapping their wings on the leather ground. I felt that the bright scene just now was a kind of harmony, and now this hazy wilderness was also a kind of harmony. From nature's point of view, it seems that nothing is not a kind of harmony. And her bright smile showed the revelation of nature.

"White clouds hiding in rocky valleys? Haven't you seen white clouds floating out? Cherishing "love" has both bright sunny snow, and dark misty rain, and also storms roaring in the dark night."

She slowly uttered each word, each sentence with rhythm. Her eyes were shining.

"The green mountains after the rain will be more beautiful!" I said.

The sky has cleared, and the distant mountains, deep forests, plains, and waves compose a new tune of harmony. She walked along the river, serenely and solemnly.

"She is a god, she is the master of nature, she is the great harmony of wisdom and beauty!"

I thought this way, and again went down the small boat with her. The small boat swayed on the waves, and the white clouds found their home in the rocky valleys!

On a Yangtze River Steamer 175

— Laizi

Late at night, when I was fast asleep, my mother suddenly woke me up:

"Hansheng, look! What's that calling? ... I just came back from the women's latrine at the stern..."

I dragged my shoes. The stewards were sprawled on the floor like dead pigs, snoring loudly; even the night watchman was leaning against the cabin door, asleep. The other passengers were also asleep, only two were still smoking opium, talking about some incomprehensible, trivial matters.

The river wind was howling. The stars in the sky were pierced by patches of thick black clouds. The waves were hitting the deck madly, desperately, sending out a deep, sharp, painful cry along with the splashing foam! My mother shrank her body and walked to the stern, where she pointed to the dark corner of the women's lavatory.

"There! Right there... there in the corner! There's some kind of sound..."

"Shall I call a steward?" I said.

"No! Go and see, there won't be a ghost... it might be a person..."

I leaned against the iron railing of the deck and stretched my head over: there was a intermittent, miserable sob coming from below, from the splash of the waves:

"Aiyo... a-aiyo..."

"Go over there! Go over there a little more and listen!" Mother said pushing my body anxiously.

"It's a person, a woman!" I replied resolutely, "She's probably hanging there with a rope, under that horizontal iron bar..."

Fifteen minutes later, following my mother's orders, I rescued that distressed woman alone, secretly and daringly.

She was heavily pregnant, a country woman of about forty years old. Her armpits and chest were almost swollen by the straps. When Mother pulled her to the dim lamplight in front of the women's lavatory door to question her, she cried quietly with a pair of small eyes with turnip flower lumps, fearfully.

"Don't cry! Silly woman! The stewards will hear you and you'll be dead..." Mother said consolingly and admonishingly.

She began to recount her life story, sadly and simply: because there was a famine in the countryside, she was dragging her pregnant belly, wanting to flee with her husband and children from Hankou to Wuhu, where she had some relatives. Without tickets, the husband and children were driven ashore by the stewards when the ship sailed, and she secretly hung there, and because it was night, she was not discovered...

Turning to me, my mother sighed a long breath and said:

"Two lives! Almost... if the strap had broken..." Turning back to her: "You hide in this lavatory for now, it will be dawn soon. We can speak well to the treasurer for you, and maybe we can take you to Wuhu..."

We went back to the cabin to sleep. Mother was still sighing for a long time!... But, as soon as dawn broke, the stewards started making a racket!

"Hansheng! Come! They're going to beat her to death..." Mother stamped her feet anxiously, pulling my ear. She didn't know what time she got up.

"Who?" I said vaguely, still half asleep.

"That pregnant woman! The one we rescued last night!... The stewards are beating her!..."

We hurried to the stern, where it had already been surrounded by a large group of early risers. A thin treasurer with glasses and wearing pajamas stood in the center, biting a cigarette leisurely, directing the stewards' interrogation. The pregnant woman bent over, shrinking into a ball, trembling, and crystal clear blood flowed from her disheveled hair. The onlookers mostly seemed to be watching a play, feeling quite happy; only a few showed "helpless" sympathy, shaking their heads and sighing!

We squeezed into the crowd, Mother following closely behind me. A one-eyed steward holding a stick showed an impatient face to us. Another, a pockmarked, fierce fellow, opened his dog-like yellow eyes and looked at the treasurer for instructions, then rushed to the trembling body of the pregnant woman and gave her a hard kick—

——To be continued——

Not Redeemed 176

— Jian Fan

Love (3) 177

— By S. Ersaijifu. Jin Siji, translated by Su Ming

As he started to clean his sheepskin coat, Prokhor said to him, "What do you need a coat for? It's summer."

Shavaka turned around and replied, "Why? So my father won't be cold."

He carefully examined the small boat, settled his weak, pale, elderly father in the stern, and prepared to depart.

"Come back in June, child," his brother said. "The things you're taking will be needed then."

"What could stop me?" Shavaka replied, spitting in his hands and immediately gripping the oars. His jaws tightened as he rowed the boat towards the yellow, dirty river.

They hadn't gone far when Shavaka asked his father where his name—Kolt—came from. He had never asked this before.

His father replied, "Probably from your grandfather."

"Then where did he get it from?" Shavaka asked again.

His father looked at him, then at the river around them, and said with a frown, "He probably got it from his grandfather."

They said no more.

On the twelfth day of their journey, just as they reached the town's hospital, his father died. Shavaka buried him in the town cemetery. He obtained a death certificate for his father, hid it deep inside his clothes, and then set off, not returning to Spiask, but continuing along the river.

He had already made up his mind. Even if his father had been alive when he arrived at the hospital and had been handed over to the doctors, he would still have done exactly the same.

As he left the town, he felt extremely upset, not because he was thinking of his dead father, but because he was thinking of the teacher, Alyosha. "Good, you girl. You have a red head, but you have a black heart."

All summer, Shavaka left Spiask, bid farewell to the girl who had hurt him, just as the reindeer farm had harmed his father, and traveled as far as possible. In the town, he used the money he earned from selling his father's clothes to buy the most essential items for a long journey. Among them were skis, scrap iron, old nails, and clumsy fishing nets. He stayed as far away from big cities as possible. He sometimes hunted, but he mostly lived by fishing, because he was careful to conserve his gunpowder and bullets.

Life 178

— Wang Yaping

Life is like a rushing torrent,

Carrying you forward,

Without stopping, never letting you look back.

Who knows where it will drift to?

Place hope in tomorrow,

Place hope in the distance,

Move forward! Steadily brace your feet,

Effortlessly raise the oar,

Let caution always be in your eyes,

Be careful of hitting reefs,

Be careful of the misty miasma,

Be careful of sudden wind and rain,

And the undulating, frightening waves.

Move forward! Seriously grip the rudder,

Let courage support your heart,

Don't fear the scorching sun,

Don't fear the piercing cold,

Don't fear the desolate night's frost and dew,

Don't fear ten thousand mountains and rivers,

Even if dark clouds cover the stars and moon,

And darkness occupies the universe,

You must keep an eye on the flashing lighthouse,

Calmly sail towards the distant voyage.

In this way, you will gain enlightenment in hardship,

And cultivate your great life in enlightenment.
